Prophethood
intermediate
6 min
Alternative Proofs for Prophethood
Sanusi presents alternative proofs for prophethood and addresses an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that prophethood can be proven through means other than miracles, such as necessary knowledge and reports from infallible sources, and how this is reconciled with the view that miracles are the primary proof.

Core Idea
Miracles aren't the only way to know a prophet; necessary knowledge and previous scriptures also prove prophethood.

In this lesson, we explore a crucial nuance in the proof of prophethood. While miracles are the standard evidence, the author clarifies that there are other valid proofs, such as the compelling knowledge that arises in a believer's heart or the testimony of earlier prophets. He also addresses a potential objection from a prominent scholar, showing that these alternatives do not contradict the primacy of miracles.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the alternative proofs
Read the passage and identify that the author is introducing a note on other ways to establish prophethood besides miracles.
The passage begins with 'تنبيه' (a note).
2
Understand the two examples
Focus on the two specific proofs: necessary knowledge (like that of Abu Bakr) and reports from infallible sources (like Torah and Gospel).
The author quotes al-Maqasid to present these examples.
3
See how Imam al-Haramayn's view is harmonized
Notice the author explains that Imam al-Haramayn's statement about miracles being the only proof applies to absolute proofs for any prophet, not to specific cases like Muhammad where other indications ultimately go back to the miracle.
This shows the author's method of reconciling different scholarly views.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبيه
على طرق أُخرى في إثبات النبوة غير المعجزة
قال في «المقاصد» : ( لا خفاء في ثبوت النبوة بخلق العلم الضروري؛ كعلم الصديق رضي الله تعالى عنه، أو بخبر من ثبتت عصمته من الكذب؛ كنصوص التوراة والإنجيل في نبوة نبينا ومولانا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم، وكإخبار موسى عليه الصلاة والسلام بنبوة هارون ويوشع عليهما الصلاة والسلام.
فما ذكره إمام الحرمين من أنه لا يمكن نصب دليل على النبوة سوى المعجزة؛ لأن ما يقدر دليلاً إن لم يكن خارقاً للعادة، أو خارقاً ولم يكن مقروناً بالدعوى لم يصلح دليلاً؛ للاتفاق على جواز وقوع الخارق من الله تعالى ابتداءً... محمول على ما يصلح دليلاً للنبوة على الإطلاق، وحجة على المنكرين بالنسبة لكل نبي عليه الصلاة والسلام، حتى الذي لا نبي قبله ولا كتاب.
وأما ما سيأتي من الاستدلال على نبوة نبينا ومولانا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم بما شاع من أخلاقه وأحواله.. فعائد إلى المعجزة
A note on alternative ways of proving prophethood besides miracles. He said in al-Maqasid: 'There is no doubt about the establishment of prophethood by the creation of necessary knowledge, like the knowledge of al-Siddiq (may Allah be pleased with him), or by the report of one whose infallibility from lying is established, such as the texts of the Torah and the Gospel regarding the prophethood of our Prophet and Master Muhammad (peace be upon him), and like the informing of Moses (peace be upon him) of the prophethood of Aaron and Joshua (peace be upon them). So what Imam al-Haramayn mentioned — that it is impossible to set up a proof for prophethood other than a miracle, because what is considered a proof, if it is not extraordinary, or if it is extraordinary but not accompanied by the claim, it is not suitable as a proof, due to the agreement on the permissibility of the occurrence of the extraordinary from Allah initially... — is to be interpreted as referring to what is suitable as a proof for prophethood absolutely, and as an argument against deniers with respect to every prophet (peace be upon him), even one before whom there was no prophet and no book. As for what will come of the inference for the prophethood of our Prophet and Master Muhammad (peace be upon him) from what is well-known of his character and circumstances... it returns to the miracle.'
Source pages p. 461

Commentary
This passage is a note (tanbih) on alternative proofs for prophethood. The author begins by stating that there are other ways to prove prophethood besides miracles: (1) the creation of necessary knowledge in a person, like the knowledge of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq that Muhammad is a prophet; (2) reports from those whose infallibility from lying is known, such as the scriptures of previous prophets (Torah and Gospel) testifying to Muhammad's prophethood, and Moses informing of Aaron and Joshua's prophethood. Then the author addresses a statement by Imam al-Haramayn (al-Juwayni) who claimed that only a miracle can be a proof for prophethood. The author explains that al-Juwayni's statement should be interpreted as referring to what can serve as an absolute proof for any prophet, including the first prophet, where no previous scripture exists. As for the specific case of Muhammad, his character and life circumstances can also be used as inference, but ultimately it goes back to the miracle (the Quran). So the author harmonizes different views.

Key Terms
إثبات النبوة
المعجزة
العلم الضروري
عصمة
إمام الحرمين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Miracles are the only way to prove prophethood.
Correction: There are other valid proofs such as necessary knowledge and reports from infallible sources, as mentioned by Sanusi.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what are the alternative proofs for prophethood besides miracles?
A) Logical deduction and intuition
B) Necessary knowledge and reports from infallible sources
C) Philosophical arguments and consensus
D) Dreams and visions

Key Takeaway
The passage teaches that while miracles are the primary proof, other valid proofs exist, and they ultimately support the same conclusion.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you possess the 'necessary knowledge' that Muhammad is a prophet, or do you rely solely on external proofs? Examine the certainty in your heart — is it as immediate as Abu Bakr's, or does it waver when doubts arise?
?
The author mentions that the Torah and Gospel testified to Muhammad's prophethood. Have you ever seriously examined those testimonies? If not, what is stopping you from seeking that confirmation?
?
Prophet Muhammad's character and circumstances are said to point to his prophethood. How does your own character reflect his teachings? Are you living in a way that would make others see the truth of his message through your actions?

The Rational and Consensus Basis of Prophetic Infallibility
Sanusi states the rational proof for infallibility from lying and the consensus for infallibility from major and base minor sins.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the infallibility of prophets from lying is known rationally through miracles, while their infallibility from major and base minor sins is established by consensus.

Core Idea
Prophets are infallible: lying is disproved by miracles, major sins by consensus.

Sanusi begins by establishing the two-fold basis for prophetic infallibility. He distinguishes between the rational proof for freedom from lying and the consensual proof for freedom from major and base minor sins. Understanding this foundation is essential before exploring the full scope of prophetic sinlessness.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening sentences
Read the first two sentences carefully. Notice the repetition: the first sentence introduces the rational proof for lying, the second adds consensus for major and base minor sins.
The author repeats 'from lying' for emphasis.
2
Identify the two types of proof
One proof is rational (the miracle), the other is based on consensus (ijma'). Ask yourself why lying requires a different proof than other sins.
3
Understand the rationale for all sins
The third part says prophets are free from all other sins because people must follow them, and God does not command disobedience. Reflect on this logical argument.
This shows that infallibility is necessary for the prophetic mission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عصمة الرسل من الكذب معلومة عقلاً بدليل المعجزة
وعصمتهم من الكذب معلومة عقلاً بدليل المعجزة، ومن كبائر المعاصي وصغائر الخسة بالإجماع، ومن سائر الذنوب؛ فإن الخلق المبعوثين هم إليهم مأمورون بالاقتداء بهم، ولا يأمر تعالى بمعصية.
هذا الذي مررنا عليه من عصمة الأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام من جميع المعاصي؛ صغيرها وكبيرها، بل ومما ليس بمعصية أصلاً؛ كالمكروهات، بل ومن المباحات أن يفعلوها لمجرد الشهوة، بل إلا بنية القربة والامتثال والاستعانة بها على طاعة المولى جل وعز.. هو التحقيق والصواب الذي لا معدل عنه إن شاء الله تعالى
وللعلماء في ذلك أقوال وبسط كثير وتفريعات مستطيلة والحق المنجلي من ذلك، ومعه السلامة بعون الله تعالى في الدين والدنيا والآخرة.. ما سمعت، وإياك أن تصغي بأذنك أو تلتفت بذهنك لخرائف المؤرخين، وأقوال جهلة المفسرين، والله حسيب
The infallibility of the messengers from lying is known rationally by the evidence of the miracle. And their infallibility from major sins and base minor sins is by consensus, and from all other sins; for the creation sent to them are commanded to follow them, and Allah does not command disobedience. This which we have passed over concerning the infallibility of the prophets (peace be upon them) from all sins, small and large, and even from that which is not a sin at all, like disliked things, and even from permissible acts that they do only for the sake of desire — rather, they do them only with the intention of drawing near, obedience, and seeking help thereby in obeying the Lord (mighty and majestic) — this is the verification and correctness from which there is no turning away, if Allah wills. And the scholars have many statements and lengthy elaboration and extensive subdivisions. But the clear truth from that, together with safety by the help of Allah in religion, this world, and the Hereafter, is what you have heard. And beware of listening with your ear or turning your mind to the absurdities of historians and the statements of ignorant exegetes. Allah suffices as a reckoner.
Source pages p. 462

Commentary
This passage defines the doctrine of prophetic infallibility ('isma). The author states that the infallibility of prophets from lying is rationally known through the evidence of the miracle. Their infallibility from major sins and base minor sins is by consensus (ijma'), and from all other sins because the people are commanded to follow them, and God does not command disobedience. Then the author expands: prophets are infallible not only from sins, but also from disliked actions, and even from permissible actions if done merely for desire; rather, their permissible actions are done with the intention of drawing near to God and for obedience. This is the correct view. The author warns against following the absurd claims of historians and ignorant exegetes.

Key Terms
عصمة الرسل
الكذب
المعجزة
كبائر المعاصي
صغائر الخسة
الإجماع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think prophets can commit minor sins.
Correction: The author explicitly states infallibility from all sins, even base minor sins, by consensus.

Checkpoint
How is the infallibility of prophets from lying known?
A) By divinely revealed book
B) By rational evidence from miracles
C) By consensus of scholars
D) By prophetic traditions

Key Takeaway
Prophets are infallible from lying by rational proof, and from major and base minor sins by consensus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If a prophet could lie, how would that undermine your trust in the divine message? This passage says the miracle proves they cannot. Is there any prophet whose truthfulness you have ever doubted? What would that mean for your faith?
?
The consensus says prophets are free from even 'base minor sins' like stealing a grain. Think of a sin you consider trivial or insignificant. If a prophet would never commit it, how does that challenge your attitude towards that sin?
?
Prophets are role models whom Allah commands us to follow. In what specific area of your life are you not following their example? What one concrete change will you make today to align closer to their sinlessness?

The Comprehensive Scope of Prophetic Infallibility
Sanusi expands prophetic infallibility to include disliked and permissible acts, and warns against contrary claims.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that prophets are infallible not only from sins but also from disliked actions and even from permissible acts done for mere desire.

Core Idea
Prophets are sinless in all actions, even permissible ones, which they only do for obedience.

Having established the basic infallibility from sins, Sanusi now expands the doctrine to its fullest extent. He explains that prophets are protected even from disliked acts and from permissible acts that are done merely out of desire. Their every action is a means of drawing near to Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the expansion passage
Notice how the author moves from sins to non-sins, categorizing disliked and permissible acts.
2
Identify the key phrase 'بل ومما ليس بمعصية أصلاً'
This clarifies that infallibility extends beyond sin to actions that are not even sinful.
3
Understand the intention behind permissible acts
The author insists prophets only do permissible acts with the intention of worship, not mere desire.
This is a strong statement about the purity of prophetic actions.
4
Note the warning against contrary views
The author explicitly rejects the absurd claims of historians and ignorant exegetes.
He warns not to listen to them.

Source Text

عصمة الرسل من الكذب معلومة عقلاً بدليل المعجزة
وعصمتهم من الكذب معلومة عقلاً بدليل المعجزة، ومن كبائر المعاصي وصغائر الخسة بالإجماع، ومن سائر الذنوب؛ فإن الخلق المبعوثين هم إليهم مأمورون بالاقتداء بهم، ولا يأمر تعالى بمعصية.

The infallibility of the messengers from lying is known rationally by the evidence of the miracle. And their infallibility from major sins and base minor sins is by consensus, and from all other sins; for the creation sent to them are commanded to follow them, and Allah does not command disobedience. This which we have passed over concerning the infallibility of the prophets (peace be upon them) from all sins, small and large, and even from that which is not a sin at all, like disliked things, and even from permissible acts that they do only for the sake of desire — rather, they do them only with the intention of drawing near, obedience, and seeking help thereby in obeying the Lord (mighty and majestic) — this is the verification and correctness from which there is no turning away, if Allah wills. And the scholars have many statements and lengthy elaboration and extensive subdivisions. But the clear truth from that, together with safety by the help of Allah in religion, this world, and the Hereafter, is what you have heard. And beware of listening with your ear or turning your mind to the absurdities of historians and the statements of ignorant exegetes. Allah suffices as a reckoner.
Source pages p. 462

Commentary
This passage defines the doctrine of prophetic infallibility ('isma). The author states that the infallibility of prophets from lying is rationally known through the evidence of the miracle. Their infallibility from major sins and base minor sins is by consensus (ijma'), and from all other sins because the people are commanded to follow them, and God does not command disobedience. This is the correct view. The author warns against following the absurd claims of historians and ignorant exegetes.

According to Sanusi, why do prophets perform permissible acts?
A) For their own desire
B) With the intention of drawing near to Allah
C) Because they have no choice
D) To set a bad example

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the prophets cannot perform even a single permissible act without intending to draw near to Allah, how many of your daily actions are done with that same sincere intention? Will you commit from this moment to renew your niyya in every permissible act—eating, sleeping, working—turning them into acts of worship?
?
The author warns you 'beware of listening with your ear or turning your mind to the absurdities of historians and ignorant exegetes' about the prophets. Have you ever accepted a story that diminished your reverence for a prophet? What practical step will you take to protect your heart from such falsehoods, starting today?
?
The prophets transformed even the most routine actions into devotion. Look at your own life: which one permissible act—such as eating, walking, or speaking—will you consciously convert into an act of obedience right now, as a first step to following their example?

Prophethood
beginner
4 min
Rational and Consensus Basis of Prophetic Infallibility
Sanusi states rational and consensus proofs for prophetic infallibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that prophetic infallibility from lying is known rationally through miracles, and infallibility from major and base minor sins is established by consensus, with a logical reason.

Core Idea
Miracles prove prophets cannot lie; consensus and reason protect them from major and base minor sins.

Sanusi begins by grounding prophetic infallibility in two solid proofs: rational evidence from miracles for protection from lying, and consensus for protection from major sins and base minor sins. He then provides the logical reason why prophets must be protected from all sin: they are role models commanding obedience.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on rational evidence
Notice the repetition: it underscores the certainty that prophets are protected from lying, proven by the miracle itself.
2
Identify the consensus and reason
See that infallibility from major sins and base minor sins is by consensus, and also from other sins because people must follow them.
3
Understand the logical argument
Since Allah commands obedience to prophets, they cannot commit sins that would contradict their role.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عصمةُ الرُّسلِ مِنَ الكذب معلومة عقلاً بدليل المعجزة ، وعصمتُهم مِنَ الكذب معلومة عقلاً بدليل المعجزة ، ومِنْ كبائر المعاصي وصغائرِ الخِسَّة بالإجماع ، ومِنْ سائرِ الذنوبِ ؛ فإِنَّ الخَلْقَ المبعوثينَ هم إليهم مأمورونَ بالاقتداء بهم ، ولا يأمرُ تعالى بمعصية . هذا الذي مررنا عليهِ مِنْ عصمةِ الأنبياء عليهم الصلاة جميع والسلامُ مِنْ جميع المعاصي ؛ صغيرها وكبيرها ، بل ومما ليس بمعصية أصلاً ؛ كالمكروهات ، بل ومِنَ المباحاتِ أنْ يفعلوها لمجرَّدِ الشهوة ، بل إلا بنيَّةِ القُرْبةِ والامتثال والاستعانة بها على طاعة المولى جلَّ وعزَّ.. هو التحقيق والصواب الذي لا مَعدِلَ عنهُ إِنْ شَاءَ اللهُ تعالى. وللعلماء في ذلكَ أقوال وبَسْطُ كثير وتفريعات مستطيلة (١) والحقُّ المنجلي مِنْ ذلكَ ، ومَعَهُ السلامةُ بعون الله تعالى في الدين والدنيا والآخرة.. ما سمعتَ ، وإِيَّاكَ أنْ تصغي بأذنكَ أو تلتفت بذهنِكَ لخرائف المؤرّخينَ ، وأقوالِ جهلة المفسرينَ ، والله حسيب مَنْ يُكدِّرُ ما صفّى الله تعالى ، والعاقلُ مَنْ لم يطلب الربح إلا بعد إحراز رأس المالِ ؛ الذي هو السلامة ممَّا يُوجِبُ الهلاك دنيا وأخرى . لا يَسْلَمُ الْحَسَبُ الرَّفِيعُ مِنَ الأَذَى حَتَّى يُرَاقَ عَلَى جَوَانِبِهِ الدَّمُ (۱) والله المستعانُ ، ولا حول ولا قوة إلا بالله . وقوله : ( صغائرِ الخِسَّةِ ( يعني بها : ما يُعَدُّ دناءةٌ في العُرْفِ ، ويدلُّ على رذالة النفس وصغرِ الهمَّةِ ؛ كسرقة لقمة والتطفيف بحبة مثلاً ، ونحو ذلكَ
The infallibility of the Messengers from lying is known rationally by the evidence of the miracle, and their infallibility from lying is known rationally by the evidence of the miracle, and from major sins and base minor sins by consensus, and from all other sins; because the people to whom they are sent are commanded to follow them, and the Exalted does not command disobedience. This that we have discussed concerning the infallibility of the prophets—peace be upon them all—from all sins, their minor and major, and even from what is not a sin at all, such as disliked things, and even from permissible acts that they would do for mere desire, but only with the intention of drawing near, obedience, and seeking assistance thereby in obedience to the Master, Mighty and Majestic—is the verification and correctness from which there is no deviation, if Allah wills. The scholars have many opinions, extensive elaboration, and lengthy ramifications (1). And the manifest truth from that, along with safety by the help of Allah in religion, this world, and the Hereafter, is what you have heard. Beware of listening with your ear or turning your mind to the absurd tales of historians and the statements of ignorant exegetes. Allah is the Reckoner of whoever disturbs what Allah has purified. The intelligent person does not seek profit except after securing capital, which is safety from what causes destruction in this world and the next. The noble lineage is not safe from harm until blood is shed on its sides (1). And Allah is the Succourer, and there is no power nor strength except with Allah. And His saying: 'base minor sins'—meaning by it: what is considered lowliness in custom, and indicates baseness of soul and pettiness of ambition, such as stealing a morsel, cheating in a grain, and the like.
Source pages p. 462

Commentary
This passage is a definition and defense of the comprehensive infallibility ('isma) of prophets. The author begins by stating that the infallibility of messengers from lying is known rationally through the evidence of miracles. Then he expands: by consensus, prophets are infallible from major sins and base minor sins (sagha'ir al-khissa), and from all other sins. The reason is that people are commanded to follow them, and Allah does not command disobedience. The author then clarifies that the correct position is that prophets are infallible from all sins, minor and major, and even from acts that are not sins at all, such as makruh (disliked) acts, and even from mubah (permissible) acts if done merely for desire. However, if prophets perform permissible acts with the intention of drawing close to Allah, obedience, and seeking help in worship, that is allowed. He asserts that this is the verified truth with no deviation. He acknowledges that scholars have other opinions but warns against listening to the fables of historians and ignorant exegetes. He then quotes a line of poetry about honor requiring sacrifice, and finally explains the phrase 'base minor sins' as things considered lowly in custom, like stealing a morsel or cheating in a grain. The passage guards against underestimating the scope of prophetic infallibility and against accepting false historical narratives that might undermine it.

Key Terms
عصمة
الرسل
الكذب
المعجزة
كبائر المعاصي
صغائر الخِسَّة
الإجماع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think prophetic infallibility is only from major sins, not minor ones.
Correction: Sanusi explicitly states prophets are infallible from major and minor (including base minor) sins by consensus.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, the infallibility of messengers from lying is known through which evidence?
A) Consensus
B) Reason and the miracle
C) Revelation alone
D) Historical reports

Key Takeaway
Prophetic infallibility is proven rationally by miracles and by consensus for major and base minor sins, grounded in the command to follow them.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If prophets are infallible from all sins, including minor ones, what does that mean for your own casual attitude toward 'small' sins? Which 'minor' sin have you normalized in your life that you would never accept in a prophet—and will you commit to removing it today?
?
The passage says people are commanded to follow the prophets, so Allah does not command disobedience. Where in your life are you claiming to follow the Prophet while tolerating a sin that contradicts that claim? What concrete step will you take before sunset to align your action with your belief?
?
Miracles prove that prophets cannot lie. Have you ever let a doubt about a prophetic teaching linger despite clear signs from Allah? What 'miracle' in your own experience demands that you trust the Prophet's truthfulness, and what will you do this week to eliminate that doubt?

Comprehensive Scope of Prophetic Infallibility
Sanusi defines the comprehensive infallibility covering all sins, disliked, and permissible acts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that prophetic infallibility covers all sins, disliked acts, and even permissible acts if done for mere desire, but allows permissible acts with good intentions.

Core Idea
Prophets are protected from all sins, disliked acts, and permissible acts done for desire, but not from permissible acts done for obedience.

Sanusi now expands his definition, moving beyond sins to include actions that are not inherently sinful. He clarifies the correct position: prophets are infallible from all sins (minor and major), disliked acts (makruhat), and even permissible acts (mubahat) if done merely for desire. However, they may perform permissible acts with the intention of drawing closer to Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the expanded definition
Notice the progression: from all sins, to disliked acts, to permissible acts. This shows the breadth of infallibility.
2
Understand the exception
Prophets can perform permissible acts if they intend nearness to Allah, obedience, or assistance in worship.
3
Affirm the correct view
Sanusi asserts that this is the verified truth from which there is no deviation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عصمةُ الرُّسلِ مِنَ الكذب معلومة عقلاً بدليل المعجزة ، وعصمتُهم مِنَ الكذب معلومة عقلاً بدليل المعجزة ، ومِنْ كبائر المعاصي وصغائرِ الخِسَّة بالإجماع ، ومِنْ سائرِ الذنوبِ ؛ فإِنَّ الخَلْقَ المبعوثينَ هم إليهم مأمورونَ بالاقتداء بهم ، ولا يأمرُ تعالى بمعصية . هذا الذي مررنا عليهِ مِنْ عصمةِ الأنبياء عليهم الصلاة جميع والسلامُ مِنْ جميع المعاصي ؛ صغيرها وكبيرها ، بل ومما ليس بمعصية أصلاً ؛ كالمكروهات ، بل ومِنَ المباحاتِ أنْ يفعلوها لمجرَّدِ الشهوة ، بل إلا بنيَّةِ القُرْبةِ والامتثال والاستعانة بها على طاعة المولى جلَّ وعزَّ.. هو التحقيق والصواب الذي لا مَعدِلَ عنهُ إِنْ شَاءَ اللهُ تعالى. وللعلماء في ذلكَ أقوال وبَسْطُ كثير وتفريعات مستطيلة (١) والحقُّ المنجلي مِنْ ذلكَ ، ومَعَهُ السلامةُ بعون الله تعالى في الدين والدنيا والآخرة.. ما سمعتَ ، وإِيَّاكَ أنْ تصغي بأذنكَ أو تلتفت بذهنِكَ لخرائف المؤرّخينَ ، وأقوالِ جهلة المفسرينَ ، والله حسيب مَنْ يُكدِّرُ ما صفّى الله تعالى ، والعاقلُ مَنْ لم يطلب الربح إلا بعد إحراز رأس المالِ ؛ الذي هو السلامة ممَّا يُوجِبُ الهلاك دنيا وأخرى . لا يَسْلَمُ الْحَسَبُ الرَّفِيعُ مِنَ الأَذَى حَتَّى يُرَاقَ عَلَى جَوَانِبِهِ الدَّمُ (۱) والله المستعانُ ، ولا حول ولا قوة إلا بالله . وقوله : ( صغائرِ الخِسَّةِ ( يعني بها : ما يُعَدُّ دناءةٌ في العُرْفِ ، ويدلُّ على رذالة النفس وصغرِ الهمَّةِ ؛ كسرقة لقمة والتطفيف بحبة مثلاً ، ونحو ذلكَ
The infallibility of the Messengers from lying is known rationally by the evidence of the miracle, and their infallibility from lying is known rationally by the evidence of the miracle, and from major sins and base minor sins by consensus, and from all other sins; because the people to whom they are sent are commanded to follow them, and the Exalted does not command disobedience. This that we have discussed concerning the infallibility of the prophets—peace be upon them all—from all sins, their minor and major, and even from what is not a sin at all, such as disliked things, and even from permissible acts that they would do for mere desire, but only with the intention of drawing near, obedience, and seeking assistance thereby in obedience to the Master, Mighty and Majestic—is the verification and correctness from which there is no deviation, if Allah wills. The scholars have many opinions, extensive elaboration, and lengthy ramifications (1). And the manifest truth from that, along with safety by the help of Allah in religion, this world, and the Hereafter, is what you have heard. Beware of listening with your ear or turning your mind to the absurd tales of historians and the statements of ignorant exegetes. Allah is the Reckoner of whoever disturbs what Allah has purified. The intelligent person does not seek profit except after securing capital, which is safety from what causes destruction in this world and the next. The noble lineage is not safe from harm until blood is shed on its sides (1). And Allah is the Succourer, and there is no power nor strength except with Allah. And His saying: 'base minor sins'—meaning by it: what is considered lowliness in custom, and indicates baseness of soul and pettiness of ambition, such as stealing a morsel, cheating in a grain, and the like.
Source pages p. 462

Commentary
This passage is a definition and defense of the comprehensive infallibility ('isma) of prophets. The author begins by stating that the infallibility of messengers from lying is known rationally through the evidence of miracles. Then he expands: by consensus, prophets are infallible from major sins and base minor sins (sagha'ir al-khissa), and from all other sins. The reason is that people are commanded to follow them, and Allah does not command disobedience. The author then clarifies that the correct position is that prophets are infallible from all sins, minor and major, and even from acts that are not sins at all, such as makruh (disliked) acts, and even from mubah (permissible) acts if done merely for desire. However, if prophets perform permissible acts with the intention of drawing close to Allah, obedience, and seeking help in worship, that is allowed. He asserts that this is the verified truth with no deviation. He acknowledges that scholars have other opinions but warns against listening to the fables of historians and ignorant exegetes. He then quotes a line of poetry about honor requiring sacrifice, and finally explains the phrase 'base minor sins' as things considered lowly in custom, like stealing a morsel or cheating in a grain. The passage guards against underestimating the scope of prophetic infallibility and against accepting false historical narratives that might undermine it.

المعاصي
صغيرها
كبيرها
المكروهات
المباحات
الشهوة
القربة
الامتثال

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think prophets can commit minor sins or disliked acts without issue.
Correction: Sanusi shows that infallibility covers even disliked acts and permissible acts done for desire; only permissible acts with good intentions are allowed.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, when can prophets perform permissible (mubah) acts?
A) Only when necessary
B) For mere desire
C) With intention of nearness to Allah
D) They cannot perform any permissible acts

Key Takeaway
Prophetic infallibility extends beyond sins to disliked and permissible acts when done for desire, but allows permissible acts with good intentions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In what areas of your life do you do permissible actions merely out of habit or desire, without any thought of drawing closer to Allah? How can you transform one such action today into an act of obedience by renewing your intention?
?
If even a prophet would not do a permissible act for mere desire, what does that reveal about the seriousness of your own intentions in everyday actions? Will you hold yourself to this standard starting now?
?
How often do you pause before a neutral action to ask: 'Am I doing this for Allah or just for myself?' Commit to doing this for one action every hour tomorrow and see how it changes your connection with your Lord.

Defending the Doctrine: Warnings and Clarifications
Sanusi warns against false narratives and defines base minor sins

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the importance of rejecting historical fables and ignorant interpretations that undermine prophetic infallibility, and learn the definition of base minor sins.

Core Idea
Guard your faith from false historical tales and ignorant exegesis; base minor sins are acts of low character like stealing a morsel.

After presenting the correct doctrine, Sanusi issues a stern warning. He advises against listening to historians and ignorant commentators who spread false narratives that tarnish prophetic dignity. He emphasizes that preserving correct belief is like safeguarding capital before seeking profit. Finally, he clarifies the meaning of 'base minor sins' as acts considered lowly in custom, such as petty theft or cheating.

Guided Path
1
Read the warning
Sanusi vehemently warns against listening to historians and ignorant exegetes who spread false stories about prophets.
2
Understand the analogy
The capital is sound belief; only after securing it can one seek profit (additional knowledge).
3
Learn the definition of base minor sins
Sanusi explains 'sagha'ir al-khissa' as actions considered lowly by custom, indicating baseness of soul.

Superiority of Prophet Muhammad and the Miracle of the Qur'an
Sanusi declares Muhammad's superiority and the Qur'an's perpetual miracle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Prophet Muhammad is considered the best of prophets and how the Qur'an serves as his enduring miracle.

Core Idea
Muhammad is the best of prophets, and the Qur'an is his everlasting miracle.

This lesson begins with Sanusi's declaration of the superiority of Prophet Muhammad over all other messengers. He then highlights that Allah supported him with countless miracles, the greatest being the Qur'an, whose inimitability remains observable today. This passage establishes both the rank of our Prophet and the ongoing evidence of his prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read and internalize the declaration
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the emphatic phrasing 'أفضل الرسل' and the triple honorifics for the Prophet.
The passage begins by asserting Muhammad's supremacy before mentioning miracles.
2
Identify the key claim about the Qur'an
Find the description of the Qur'an as 'أفضلها القرآن العظيم' and its attribute 'مُدْرَك بِالعِيان'. Understand that this means its miraculous nature is directly observable.
This contrasts with other miracles that were witnessed only at the time of the Prophet.
3
Reflect on the significance
Consider why the Qur'an's inimitability is described as ongoing and perceptible to all, and how this strengthens faith in Muhammad's prophethood.
The passage concludes that this is clear to every divinely guided person.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أفضلُ الرُّسل نبينا وسيدنا ومولانا محمد عليه الصلاة والسلام ، وذكر بعض معجزاتِهِ ] وأفضلهم نبينا وسيدنا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ، بعثَهُ الله سبحانَهُ إلى أهلِ الأَرضِ كافَّةً ، وأَيَّدَهُ بمعجزات لا حصر لها، وأفضلها القرآن العظيم الذي إعجازه للخَلْقِ مُدْرَكُ بِالعِيانِ إلى الآنَ لا خفاءَ لكلِّ مُوفَّقٍ : أنَّ سيّدَنا ومولانا محمداً رسولُ اللهِ
The best of the Messengers is our Prophet, our Master, and our Patron Muhammad, peace and blessings be upon him. And mention of some of his miracles: And the best of them is our Prophet, our Master, and our Patron Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. Allah, glorified be He, sent him to all the people of the earth, and supported him with countless miracles. The best of them is the Mighty Qur'an, whose inimitability for creation is perceived by direct observation until now. It is no secret to every divinely guided person that our Master and Patron Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah.
Source pages p. 463

Commentary
This passage is a declaration of the superiority of Prophet Muhammad over all other prophets and a mention of his miracles. The author states that the best of the messengers is our Prophet Muhammad, and then mentions some of his miracles. He emphasizes that Allah sent him to all mankind universally, not just to a specific people. He supported him with countless miracles, the greatest of which is the Noble Qur'an. The inimitability (i'jaz) of the Qur'an is perceptible by direct observation (bi al-'iyan) up to the present time. This means that the Qur'an's miraculous nature is evident and ongoing, not limited to the time of revelation. The author concludes that it is clear to every rightly guided person that Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah. The passage serves to affirm Muhammad's prophethood and the Qur'an as a perpetual miracle.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the miracles of prophets are only historical events that cannot be witnessed today.
Correction: Sanusi emphasizes that the Qur'an's inimitability is continuously observable ('perceived by direct observation until now'), making it an ongoing miracle.

Checkpoint

A) The splitting of the moon
B) The Isra' and Mi'raj
C) The Qur'an

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
The passage says it is no secret to every divinely guided person that Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah. If you consider yourself guided, does your daily life reflect that certainty? What would change if you truly lived as if this fact were as evident as the sun?

The Proof of Muhammad's Prophethood: Claim and Miracle
Author presents the proof of Muhammad's prophethood via claim and miracle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the standard kalam proof for Muhammad's prophethood, which requires both his claim of prophethood and his manifestation of miracles.

Core Idea
A true prophet must both claim prophethood and perform miracles—Muhammad did both.

This passage presents the foundational argument for Muhammad's prophethood used in Sunni kalam. The author establishes that prophethood is proven by two inseparable elements: a public claim and supernatural miracles. He then shows how both are verified in the case of Muhammad, especially through the Quran and other widely transmitted miracles.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the Proposition
The author begins by praising Muhammad and stating his universal mission. Then he notes that only some Jews and Christians denied his prophethood.
This sets the stage for the proof.
2
Identify the Proof Structure
The core proof is a syllogism: Muhammad claimed prophethood and performed miracles; anyone who does that is a prophet.
This is the logical backbone.
3
Examine the Evidence for the Claim
The claim of prophethood is described as 'known by necessity'—it was publicly made and widely known.
This addresses the first premise.
4
Examine the Evidence for the Miracles
Three types of miracles are listed: the Quran, reports of the unseen, and numerous extraordinary acts. Their collective transmission reaches tawatur (widespread).
This supports the second premise.
5
Reflect on the Implication
This proof is directed against skeptics, particularly those Jews and Christians who denied, showing that the evidence is overwhelming.
Consider how this answers their objection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأفضلهم نبينا وسيدنا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ، بعثَهُ الله سبحانَهُ إلى أهلِ الأَرضِ كافَّةً، وأَيَّدَهُ بمعجزات لا حصر لها، وأفضلها القرآن العظيم الذي إعجازه للخَلْقِ مُدْرَكُ بِالعِيانِ إلى الآنَ لا خفاءَ لكلِّ مُوفَّقٍ : أنَّ سيّدَنا ومولانا محمداً رسولُ اللهِ ، أرسلَه بالهدى ودين الحق ولم يخالف في ذلكَ مِنْ أهل المِلَل والأديانِ إلا البعضُ مِنَ اليهود والنصارى ، وحُجَّتُنا : أَنَّهُ عليهِ الصلاةُ والسلام ادعى النبوَّةَ ، وأظهر المعجزة ؛ وكلُّ مَنْ كانَ كذلك فهو نبي . أما دعواه النبوَّةَ والرسالة إلى الخَلْقِ : فأمر معلوم بالضرورة . وأمَّا إظهاره للمعجزة : فلأنَّهُ أتى بالقرآنِ ، وأخبر بالمغيَّباتِ وأظهر أفعالاً كثيرةً تَخرجُ عنِ الحَصْرِ على خلاف المعتادِ ، بلغَتْ جملتها حد التواتر وإنْ كانَ تفاصيل بعضها مِنَ الأَحادِ .
And the best of them is our Prophet, our Master, and our Patron Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace. God, glorified be He, sent him to all the people of the earth, and supported him with miracles without limit, the greatest of which is the Mighty Quran, whose inimitability for creation is perceived by sight until now. It is no secret to every successful person that our Master and Patron Muhammad is the Messenger of God; He sent him with guidance and the religion of truth. And none among the people of religions and faiths disagreed with that except some of the Jews and Christians. And our proof: that he, peace be upon him, claimed prophethood and manifested the miracle; and whoever is like that is a prophet. As for his claim of prophethood and messengership to creation, it is a matter known by necessity. And as for his manifestation of the miracle: it is because he brought the Quran, and informed of unseen things, and manifested numerous acts beyond enumeration, contrary to the usual course of things; their totality reached the level of tawatur (widespread transmission) although the details of some of them are from singular reports.
Source pages p. 463

Commentary
This passage is a proof of the prophethood of Muhammad. It first praises him as the best of messengers, sent to all people, and notes his countless miracles, especially the Quran whose inimitability is evident. Then it states that only some Jews and Christians deny his prophethood. The proof is presented as a syllogism: Muhammad claimed prophethood and performed miracles; anyone who does this is a prophet. The claim is known by necessity (as it was universally known). The miracles are specified: the Quran, reports of the unseen, and numerous extraordinary acts that are widely transmitted (tawatur) in total, even if some details are from singular reports. This is a standard kalam argument for prophethood.

Key Terms
معجزة
نبوة
تواتر
أحاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Miracles alone suffice to prove prophethood.
Correction: The author explicitly requires both claim of prophethood and manifestation of miracles; miracles without claim would not prove a prophet.

Checkpoint
What is the proof given for Muhammad's prophethood?
A) His miracles alone
B) His claim alone
C) His claim of prophethood and manifestation of miracles
D) The consensus of all people

Key Takeaway
Muhammad's prophethood is proven by his public claim and the clear miracles he brought, especially the Quran.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
The proof hinges on both claim and miracle together. Are you living as if you have accepted that proof, or are you still holding back one aspect—perhaps acknowledging the miracle but rejecting the claim's authority over your life? What would change if you fully submitted?

Proof of Muhammad's Prophethood
Sanusi summarizes the proof of Muhammad's prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical proof for Muhammad's prophethood based on his claim and miracles, and why the multiplicity of miracles establishes certainty.

Core Idea
Muhammad's claim plus miracles proves his prophethood.

Sanusi provides a clear and concise proof for the prophethood of Muhammad (peace be upon him). He states that all religious communities, except some Jews and Christians, accept his prophethood. The proof is simple: he claimed prophethood and performed miracles. Anyone who does that is a prophet. This lesson will examine that argument and the evidence for the miracles.

Guided Path
1
Understand the proof structure
Notice that Sanusi presents a conditional proof: if someone claims prophethood and manifests miracles, then he is a prophet. Then he applies it to Muhammad.
The key is the combination of claim and miracle.
2
Examine the evidence for the claim
The claim of prophethood is known by necessity – it is historically established beyond doubt. Muhammad publicly declared his prophethood and his message spread widely.
3
Examine the evidence for miracles
Sanusi lists the Qur'an, news of the unseen, and numerous extraordinary acts. Their cumulative frequency (tawatur) yields certainty, even if individual details are from ahad reports.
Tawatur means mass transmission, which gives certain knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم يخالف في ذلك من أهل الملل والأديان إلا البعض من اليهود والنصارى، وحجتنا: أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام ادعى النبوة، وأظهر المعجزة؛ وكل من كان كذلك فهو نبي. أما دعواه النبوة والرسالة إلى الخلق: فأمر معلوم بالضرورة. وأما إظهاره للمعجزة: فلأنه أتى بالقرآن، وأخبر بالمغيبات وأظهر أفعالا كثيرة تخرج عن الحصر على خلاف المعتاد، بلغت جملتها حد التواتر وإن كان تفاصيل بعضها من الأحاد.
And no one from the people of religions and faiths disagreed with that except some of the Jews and Christians. Our proof: that he (peace and blessings be upon him) claimed prophethood and manifested the miracle; and whoever is like that is a prophet. As for his claim of prophethood and messenger-ship to the creation: it is a matter known by necessity. As for his manifestation of the miracle: because he brought the Qur'an, and informed of unseen things, and manifested many actions that exceed enumeration, contrary to custom, whose totality reached the level of tawatur even if the details of some of them are from ahad reports.
Source pages p. 464

Commentary
This passage is a concise proof for the prophethood of Muhammad (peace be upon him). Sanusi begins by noting that except for some Jews and Christians, all religious communities agree on his prophethood. He then presents the proof: Muhammad claimed prophethood and performed miracles; anyone who does that is a prophet. The claim of prophethood is known by necessity (i.e., historically established). The manifestation of miracles is proven specifically by the Qur'an, by his news of the unseen, and by numerous extraordinary acts. Their cumulative frequency (tawatur) establishes certainty, even if some individual details come from isolated (ahad) reports.

Key Terms
النبوة
المعجزة
التواتر
الأحاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the proof for prophethood requires a single clear miracle, and if that is questioned then the proof fails.
Correction: Sanusi shows that the proof is based on the conjunction of claim and multiple miracles, and the cumulative evidence from many miracles (tawatur) provides certainty.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what is the proof for Muhammad's prophethood?
A) He claimed prophethood alone.
B) He performed miracles alone.
C) He claimed prophethood and performed miracles.
D) The consensus of Jews and Christians.

Key Takeaway
The proof of Muhammad's prophethood lies in his claim of prophethood and his manifestation of multiple miracles, which collectively establish certainty.

Repetition in the Quran: A Refutation
Sanusi refutes the claim that the Quran contains defective repetition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why repetition in the Quran is not a defect but a rhetorical strength, and how Sanusi refutes the objection.

Core Idea
Repetition in the Quran is eloquence, not error.

Critics sometimes claim the Quran contains meaningless repetition. Sanusi responds by showing that such repetition serves different contexts and purposes, and that scholars of eloquence have already explained its beauties. This lesson unpacks his refutation and helps you appreciate the Quran's rhetorical artistry.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the passage that presents the critics' claim and their examples of repetition in the Quran.
The examples include the story of Pharaoh and repeated refrains like 'So which of the favors of your Lord would you deny?'
2
Understand Sanusi's refutation
Sanusi argues that the repetition is due to the critics' poor understanding of speech contexts and that the repetitions are actually beautiful.
He refers to scholars of badi', meanings, and eloquence who have explained these beauties.
3
Reflect on the lesson's significance
Consider how this refutation defends the Quran's eloquence and why context matters in evaluating speech.
This helps guard against hasty criticisms of scripture.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها : أن قالوا أتلفَ اللهُ رأيهم : إِنَّ فيه عيب التكرار ؛ كإعادةِ قصَّةِ فرعون في عدة مواضع ، وكإعادة : ﴿ فَبِأَيِّ آلَاءِ رَبِّكُمَا تُكَذِّبَانِ ﴾ ، ووَيْلٌ يَوْمَيذٍ لِلْمُكَذِّبِينَ في سورة ( الرحمن ) و ( المرسلات ) . والرد عليهم : بأنَّ ذلكَ مِنْ سوء فهمهم ، وعدم إدراكهم لأحوالِ الكلام ، وما يطابقها في كلّ محلّ على التمامِ ، ومحاسنُ ما ذُكِرَ مِنْ ذلكَ وأمثالِهِ ممَّا وقعَ في القرآنِ : قد قرَّرَها أكمل تقريرٍ علماء البديع ، و فرسان المعاني ، وأئمة البيانِ
And among them is that they said—may Allah destroy their opinion—: 'Indeed in it is the defect of repetition, like the repetition of the story of Pharaoh in several places, and like the repetition of "So which of the favors of your Lord would you deny?" and "Woe that Day to the deniers" in Surah ar-Rahman and al-Mursalat.' The refutation against them is that that is due to their poor understanding and their lack of comprehension of the states of speech and what corresponds to them in each place completely; and the beauties of what has been mentioned of that and its likes from what occurred in the Quran—the scholars of badi', the champions of meanings, and the imams of eloquence have established them in the most complete manner.
Source pages p. 475

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an objection against the Quran. The objectors claim that the Quran contains a defect: repetition, citing examples such as the repeated story of Pharaoh and repeated refrains like 'So which of the favors of your Lord would you deny?' and 'Woe that Day to the deniers.' The refutation argues that this is due to the objectors' poor understanding and failure to grasp the varying contexts of speech. The beauties of such repetitions have been fully expounded by experts in badi', meanings, and eloquence. Thus, repetition is a literary virtue, not a flaw.

Key Terms
تكرار
بديع
معاني
بيان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All repetition in any text is a defect and a sign of poor eloquence.
Correction: Repetition can be a deliberate rhetorical device serving contextual and pedagogical purposes, as demonstrated by Quranic repetitions.

Checkpoint

A) It is a defect due to lack of eloquence.
B) It is due to different contexts and rhetorical purposes.
C) It is a mistake by the scribes.
D) It is to fill space.

Key Takeaway
Repetition in the Quran is a deliberate rhetorical tool that enhances meaning, not a flaw.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Refuting the Qira'at Objection
Sanusi refutes the claim that differing qira'at contradict Quran 4:82.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi refutes the claim that over twelve thousand qira'at variations contradict the Quran's statement that it contains no difference.

Core Idea
The Quran's 'no difference' means no disparity in eloquence, not uniformity of recitation.

Having established the Quran's inimitability, Sanusi now addresses a second objection: the existence of multiple qira'at (readings) appears to contradict the verse that says the Quran has no 'difference'. This objection is serious because it questions the divine origin of the Quran. In this passage, Sanusi explains the precise meaning of 'difference' in the verse, showing that the qira'at are, in fact, a sign of eloquence and divine preservation, not a flaw.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Start by reading the Arabic text of the objection. Notice how the objectors cite verse 4:82 and claim that the multitude of qira'at variations—over twelve thousand—proves the Quran has difference.
The number 'twelve thousand' is a well-known traditional figure; it emphasizes the scale of variation.
2
Identify Sanusi's refutation
Sanusi's response is concise. He redefines the term 'difference' (ikhtilaf) in the verse. Identify what he says the negated difference actually refers to.
Pay attention to the phrase 'التفاوت في مراتب البلاغة' (disparity in degrees of eloquence).
3
Understand the key distinction
Contrast the objection's assumption (that any variation is contradiction) with Sanusi's clarification (only disparity in eloquence is negated). Reflect on why this distinction resolves the conflict.
All qira'at are equally eloquent and miraculous, so they do not contradict the verse.
4
Connect to the broader argument
Consider how this refutation supports the Quran's claim of divine origin. If the qira'at were from other than Allah, they would indeed show uneven quality—but they are all equally perfect.
This ties back to the proof of prophethood through Quranic inimitability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها : أن قالوا فضحهم الله تعالى وهتك سترهم في الدنيا والآخرة : إنَّ فيهِ قولَهُ تعالى : ﴿ وَلَوْ كَانَ مِنْ عِندِ غَيْرِ اللَّهِ لَوَجَدُوا فِيهِ اخْتِلَافًا كَثِيرًا ﴾ [النساء : ۸۲]، وأنتَ تجد فيه الاختلاف المسموعَ بينَ أصحاب القراءة ما يربي على اثني عشر ألفاً . والرد عليهم : أنَّ المراد بالاختلافِ المنفي هو التفاوت في مراتبِ البلاغةِ ؛ بحيثُ يكونُ بعضُه قاصراً عن مرتبة الإعجاز .
And among them is that they said—may Allah disgrace them and expose their veil in this world and the Hereafter—: 'Indeed in it is His saying: "And if it had been from other than Allah, they would have found within it much difference" [an-Nisa 4:82]; yet you find in it the heard difference among the people of qira'ah reaching over twelve thousand [variations].' The refutation against them is that what is meant by the negated difference is disparity in degrees of eloquence, such that some of it falls short of the level of inimitability.
Source pages p. 475

Commentary
This passage refutes a second objection. The objectors cite verse 4:82 which says that if the Quran were not from Allah, there would be many discrepancies. Yet they claim that over twelve thousand variations exist among the qira'at. The refutation clarifies that the 'difference' negated in the verse refers to disparity in eloquence and rhetorical quality, not the presence of multiple authentic recitations. Thus, the existing qira'at are all equally eloquent and miraculous, so there is no contradiction.

Key Terms
اختلاف القراءات
بلاغة
إعجاز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The existence of multiple qira'at proves the Quran contains contradictions and is not from Allah.
Correction: The qira'at are all equally eloquent and miraculous; the Quran only denies disparity in eloquence, not variety in recitation.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what kind of 'difference' does the Quran deny in verse 4:82?
A) Difference in wording among the qira'at.
B) Difference in rulings between verses.
C) Disparity in eloquence and rhetorical quality.
D) Difference in meanings.

Key Takeaway
The Quran's denial of 'difference' refers to disparity in eloquence, not the existence of multiple qira'at, which are all equally miraculous.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Refuting the Claim of Contradiction in the Quran
Sanusi refutes the claim of contradiction with two reconciliations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how apparent contradictions in the Quran are resolved through proper interpretation, using the examples of questioning and Hell's food.

Core Idea
Apparent contradictions in the Quran dissolve when context and purpose are understood.

Critics often claim the Quran contains contradictions, pointing to verses that seem to conflict. Imam Sanusi addresses this objection by showing that the conditions for true contradiction are absent, and he provides specific reconciliations from tafsir. This lesson examines his method for resolving two famous pairs of verses.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the examples given.
2
Identify the two pairs of verses
The passage mentions two apparent contradictions: one about being questioned, another about Hell's food. Find them and note how they seem to conflict.
One pair is from Surah ar-Rahman and al-Hijr; the other from al-Ghashiyah and al-Haqqah.
3
Understand the reconciliations
Sanusi presents two reconciliations. For the questioning verses, the type of questioning differs. For the food verses, the foods are either for different groups or are the same. Understand these explanations.
Focus on why the negation of one type does not contradict the affirmation of another.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها : أن قالوا شتَّتَ اللهُ تعالى شملهم ، وهَدَمَ أُشهُم ، وأبطل حراكهم وحِسَّهم : إِنَّ فِيهِ تناقضاً ؛ كقوله تعالى : ﴿ فَوْمَذٍ لَّا يَسْتَلُ مَن ذَنْبِهِ إنس ولا جان ﴾ [الرحمن : ٣٩]، مع قوله تعالى : ﴿ فَوَرَبِّكَ لَنَستَلَنَّهُمْ أَجْمَعِينَ * عَمَّا كَانُوا يَعْمَلُونَ ﴾ [الحجر : ۹۲-۹۳) ، وكقوله تعالى : ( لَيْسَ لَمْ طَعَامُ إِلَّا مِن ضَرِيع ﴾ [الغاشية : ٦]، مع قوله تعالى : ﴿ وَلَا طَعَامُ إِلَّا مِنْ غِسْلِينِ ﴾ [الحاقة : ١٣٦، إلى غير ذلكَ مِنْ مواضع يُتوهَّمُ فيها تنافي الكلامين . والرد عليهم : بمنع وجودِ شرائط التناقض ، وقد بُيِّنَ ذلك على التفصيل التام في كتب التفسير . فأحد ما قيل في الجمع بين الآيتين السابقتين : أنَّ السؤال المثبت هو سؤال التوبيخ والإيقاف على خبائث الأعمال ، والسؤال المنفي هو سؤال الاستعلام والاستخبارِ ، ولا شكّ أنَّهُ مستحيل على الله تعالى ؛ لأنَّه العالم بكل شيء . وأحد ما قيل في الجمع بين الأخيرتين بناء على أنَّ الغسلينَ مباين في المعنى للضريع ، وأنَّ الغِسلين صديد أهل النار وما يجري مِنْ جراحهم ، والضريع شجرةُ الزَّقُوم ، أو شوك فيها ، أو نبت فيها : أنَّ الغِسلينَ طعام لقوم لا يأكلون غيرَهُ ، والضريع طعام لقوم آخرين لا يأكلون غيرَهُ ، وأمَّا مَنْ قالَ : إِنَّ الضريعَ والغسلينَ بمعنى واحدٍ ، والغسلين يجري مِنَ الضريع .. فلا إشكال حينئذ
And among them is that they said—may Allah Most High scatter their gatherings, demolish their edifices, and nullify their movement and senses—: 'Indeed in it is contradiction, like His saying: "Then on that Day, neither man nor jinn will be asked about his sin" [ar-Rahman 55:39], along with His saying: "So by your Lord, We will surely question them all about what they used to do" [al-Hijr 15:92-93], and like His saying: "No food will there be for them except from dari'" [al-Ghashiyah 88:6], along with His saying: "And no food except from ghislin" [al-Haqqah 69:36], and other instances where the two statements are supposed to be contradictory.' The refutation against them is by denying the existence of the conditions of contradiction, and that has been explained in full detail in books of tafsir. One thing said in reconciliation of the first two verses is that the affirmed questioning is questioning of rebuke and exposing evil deeds, while the negated questioning is questioning of inquiry and asking for information; there is no doubt that this is impossible for Allah because He is knower of all things. One thing said in reconciliation of the last two verses—based on the view that ghislin is different in meaning from dari', and that ghislin is the pus of the people of Hell and what flows from their wounds, while dari' is the tree of Zaqqum, or thorns in it, or a plant in it—is that ghislin is food for a people who eat nothing else, and dari' is food for another people who eat nothing else. As for those who say that dari' and ghislin are the same thing, and that ghislin flows from dari', then there is no problem at all.
Source pages p. 475

Commentary
This passage refutes a third objection: that the Quran contains contradictions. Four examples are given: two verses about questioning sinners (one denies questioning, the other affirms it), and two verses about the food of Hell (one says dari', the other ghislin). The refutation first states that the conditions for true contradiction are absent, and that detailed reconciliations are found in tafsir works. Then two reconciliations are presented: (1) For the questioning verses, the negated questioning is one of inquiry (since Allah knows all), while the affirmed questioning is for rebuke. (2) For the food verses, one explanation is that ghislin and dari' are distinct foods for different groups; another view holds they are the same, so no conflict. Thus, apparent contradictions are resolved through proper interpretation.

Key Terms
تناقض
تفسير
ضريع
غسلين
سؤال توبيخ
سؤال استعلام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Quran contains actual logical contradictions that cannot be resolved.
Correction: Apparent contradictions are resolved by understanding the specific contexts, types of actions, and referents, as shown in classical tafsir.

Checkpoint
How does Sanusi reconcile the two verses about questioning on the Day of Judgment?
A) One verse abrogates the other.
B) The negated questioning is for inquiry, the affirmed is for rebuke.
C) The verses apply to different groups of people.
D) The questioning is metaphorical.

Key Takeaway
Apparent contradictions in the Quran are resolved by understanding the specific contexts and purposes of each verse, as demonstrated in classical tafsir.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a verse that seems difficult to understand, do you trust that there is a reconciliation, or do you allow doubt to creep in? This lesson shows that scholars immediately seek a resolution. Where is your heart in moments of confusion?
?
The Quran repeatedly commands you to reflect on its meanings. Have you ever dismissed a verse as contradictory instead of seeking deeper knowledge? What would it take for you to adopt the humility of the scholars who assume coherence even when they don't see it?
?
If Allah questioned you about your deeds, would you fear the rebuke or welcome the inquiry? This lesson distinguishes between two types of questioning. Which one do you truly expect on that Day, and how does that shape your actions now?

Miracles: News of the Unseen
Sanusi classifies the second type of miracles as reports of past and future unseen events.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's accurate reports of past and future unseen events constitute a distinct type of miracle proving his prophethood.

Core Idea
The Prophet's knowledge of the unseen is a clear miracle.

Sanusi now turns to a second category of miracles: the Prophet's reports of events that no human could naturally know. These include detailed accounts of past nations and accurate predictions of future events. This lesson examines how such reports serve as supernatural proof of his prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then its English translation. Notice how Sanusi structures the classification into past and future unseen.
2
Identify the two subtypes
The passage divides news of the unseen into past (al-māḍiyah) and future (al-mustaqbilah). Find the examples given for each.
Past: stories of prophets; Future: Quranic prophecies like the Roman victory.
3
Understand the miraculous nature
Reflect on why these reports are miraculous: the Prophet had no prior education or access to scriptures, yet narrated detailed accounts. The future predictions came true exactly.
See the Quranic verse Hūd 49 as proof for past unseen.
4
Answer the checkpoint
Test your understanding by answering the multiple-choice question. The answer is directly from the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النوع الثاني مِنْ أنواع معجزاتِهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ : إخبارُهُ عَنِ الغيوب الماضية والمستقبلة. أما الماضيةُ : فقصَّةُ موسى عليه السلام وفرعونَ ، وقصَّةُ يوسف وإبراهيم ، ونوحٍ ، ولوط ، عليهم الصلاة والسلام ، وغيرهم على تفاصيلها وطُولِها ، مِنْ غيرِ سماع قطُّ مِنْ أحدٍ ، ولا تَلَقَّ مِنْ كتاب ، كما أشير إليه بقولِهِ تعالى : تِلْكَ مِنْ أَنْبَاءِ الْغَيْبِ نُوحِيهَا إِلَيْكَ ما كُنتَ تَعْلَمُها أَنتَ وَلَا قَوْمُكَ مِن قَبْلِ هَذَا ﴾ [هود : ٤٩] ، ووقع لهُ مِنْ أمثال هذا ممَّا ليس في القرآن كثير. وأمَّا المستقبلة : فمنها ما في القرآن : كقوله تعالى : ( وَعَدَكُمُ اللهُ مَغَانِمَ كَثِيرَةً تَأْخُذُونَهَا) (الفتح : ٢٠] . الم * غُلِبَتِ الرُّومُ فِي أَدْنَى الْأَرْضِ ...) إلى قوله : ( وَعْدَ اللَّهِ لَا يُخلفُ اللهُ وَعْدَهُ ﴾ [الروم : ١-٦].
The second type of his miracles, may God bless him and grant him peace, is his informing of the unseen (ghuyūb) past and future. As for the past: the story of Moses, peace be upon him, and Pharaoh, and the story of Joseph, Abraham, Noah, Lot, peace be upon them all, and others, with their details and length, without having heard at all from anyone, nor having learned from a book, as indicated by His saying, the Most High: 'That is from the news of the unseen which We reveal to you; you did not know it, nor did your people, before this' [Hūd 49]. And there occurred for him many similar things not in the Quran. As for the future: among them is what is in the Quran, such as His saying, the Most High: 'God has promised you much booty that you will take' [al-Fatḥ 20]; and 'Alif Lām Mīm. The Romans have been defeated in the nearest land...' up to His saying: '[That is] the promise of God; God does not fail in His promise' [al-Rūm 1-6].
Source pages p. 480

Commentary
This passage is a classification and proof. Sanusi identifies the second type of the Prophet's ﷺ miracles as his reports of the unseen (al-ghuyūb), both past and future. For past unseen events, he cites the detailed stories of earlier prophets and nations that the Prophet ﷺ narrated without any prior learning, as confirmed by Quranic verse Hūd 49. He notes that many such reports exist outside the Quran as well. For future unseen events, he gives two Quranic examples: the promise of future conquest (Fatḥ 20) and the prophecy of the Romans' victory after defeat (Rūm 1-6). These accurate reports, which could not have been known naturally, serve as clear miracles proving his prophethood.

Key Terms
معجزات
إخبار عن الغيوب
الغيوب الماضية
الغيوب المستقبلة
أنباء الغيب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the Quran is the only miracle of the Prophet.
Correction: Sanusi shows that the Prophet's reports of the unseen, both in and outside the Quran, are also miracles.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what makes the Prophet's reports of past events a miracle?
A) They were written in beautiful poetry.
B) He learned them from Jews and Christians.
C) He narrated them in detail without ever hearing or learning them from anyone.
D) They are all in the Quran.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's accurate reports of the unseen, past and future, are a clear miracle proving his prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You read that the Prophet knew the detailed stories of previous prophets without ever reading a book. You have the Quran in your hands. When you read these stories, do you feel the same certainty as if you were there? Or do you read them as mere tales? What would change if you truly believed they are news from the Unseen revealed to him?
?
The Prophet foretold that the Romans would defeat the Persians after being defeated, and it happened. He also promised you that the righteous will inherit Paradise. Which of his prophecies do you find harder to trust: the one already fulfilled or the one yet to come? Why? And how does your answer affect your daily actions?
?
The Prophet reported unseen matters not only in the Quran but also outside it. You claim to follow him, but how much of his sunnah—including his warnings about the grave and the hereafter—do you take as seriously as you take tomorrow's schedule? What would change if you treated every hadith about the unseen as a current event?

Prophecies of the Past Unseen as Miracles
Sanusi enumerates the second type of miracle: prophecies of past unseen events.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Prophet's accurate accounts of past events are considered a miraculous sign of his prophethood.

Core Idea
The Prophet's knowledge of past history was a miracle from Allah.

In this passage, Sanusi continues his enumeration of miracles by describing the second type: prophecies of the unseen. He focuses on accounts of past prophets, which the Prophet relayed in detail without any human source. This lesson explores how these accurate reports serve as evidence of divine revelation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the translation. Let Sanusi's words and the Quranic verse resonate.
Notice the phrase 'إخباره عن الغيوب الماضية' as the key category.
2
Identify the two subcategories
Sanusi divides 'informing of the unseen' into past and future. Then he elaborates on the past with examples of prophets.
The future is mentioned but not detailed here.
3
Examine the evidence
Reflect on the Quranic verse from Surah Hud (11:49) which explicitly states these stories were unknown to the Prophet and his people.
This verse is a direct proof that the knowledge was from Allah.
4
Understand the miraculous nature
Consider that the Prophet was unlettered and never studied scriptures or heard these stories from anyone. His accurate, detailed narratives are a miracle.
Sanusi adds that many similar non-Quranic reports also occurred.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النوع الثاني من أنواع معجزاته صلى الله عليه وسلم: إخباره عن الغيوب الماضية والمستقبلة. أما الماضية: فقصة موسى عليه السلام وفرعون، وقصة يوسف وإبراهيم، ونوح، ولوط، عليهم الصلاة والسلام، وغيرهم على تفاصيلها وطولها، من غير سماع قط من أحد، ولا تلق من كتاب، كما أشير إليه بقوله تعالى: {تِلْكَ مِنْ أَنْبَاءِ الْغَيْبِ نُوحِيهَا إِلَيْكَ مَا كُنْتَ تَعْلَمُهَا أَنْتَ وَلَا قَوْمُكَ مِنْ قَبْلِ هَذَا} [هود: 49]، ووقع له من أمثال هذا مما ليس في القرآن كثير.
The second type of his miracles, may God bless him and grant him peace: his informing of the hidden past and future. As for the past: the story of Moses, peace be upon him, and Pharaoh, and the story of Joseph, Abraham, Noah, Lot, peace be upon them, and others in their detail and length, without ever hearing from anyone, nor receiving from a book, as indicated by His saying, the Exalted: {That is from the news of the unseen which We reveal to you; you did not know them, neither you nor your people, before this} [Hud: 49], and there occurred to him many similar things not in the Quran.
Source pages p. 480

Commentary
This passage classifies and defines the second type of the Prophet's miracles: prophecies of the unseen. Sanusi first states the general category: informing of past and future hidden matters. Then he specifies the past unseen: the detailed stories of earlier prophets (Moses, Joseph, Abraham, Noah, Lot) which were revealed to the Prophet without him having studied any book or heard them from anyone. He then cites Quranic evidence from Surah Hud (verse 49) explicitly stating that these were unknown to the Prophet and his people. Finally, he notes that many such non-Quranic reports also occurred (through hadith). The passage thus establishes that these accurate accounts of the past are miraculous because they came from an unlettered prophet.

Key Terms
إخباره عن الغيوب
الغيوب الماضية
أنباء الغيب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Prophet learned these stories from Jewish or Christian sources.
Correction: Sanusi clarifies that the Prophet never heard them from anyone nor received them from a book, indicating divine revelation.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what makes the Prophet's accounts of past prophets miraculous?
A) They were revealed in eloquent Arabic.
B) They were detailed and long but he never learned them from any source.
C) They were confirmed by later historians.
D) They were written in a book before him.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's accurate knowledge of past events, which he could not have acquired naturally, is a clear miracle confirming his prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the detailed stories of past prophets in the Quran, do you truly recognize them as a direct miracle from Allah confirming the Prophet's truthfulness, or do you take them for granted as mere historical accounts? How can you deepen your appreciation of this miracle in your daily recitation?
?
If you were to meet someone who claims the Prophet learned these stories from Jewish or Christian sources, how would your heart react? Would you be shaken, or would you be certain of the miraculous proof? What is the state of your certainty (yaqin) regarding the Prophet's unlettered status, and what steps will you take to strengthen it?
?
The Prophet knew details of past nations without any human teacher. How does this reality challenge your reliance on human sources of knowledge alone? In what area of your life do you need to trust Allah's revelation more than human opinions, starting today?
