Quranic Prophecies as Miracles
Sanusi lists Quranic verses that contain predictions of future events.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quran itself contains multiple future prophecies that serve as miracles proving Muhammad's prophethood.

Core Idea
The Quran predicted specific events—all fulfilled exactly—proving divine origin.

Sanusi continues his classification of miracles by turning to the second type: prophecies of future events. He first cites verses from the Quran that foretold specific occurrences, all of which later came true. This passage demonstrates that the Prophet's knowledge of the unseen was not limited to his own time but extended to future events.

Guided Path
1
Read the list of verses
Read through the verses Sanusi cites, noting the predicted event in each verse.
There are eleven verses or verse sets.
2
Understand the fulfillment
For each verse, recall or research how the prediction was fulfilled in Islamic history.
For example, the promise of booty was fulfilled at Khaybar.
3
Appreciate the cumulative proof
Reflect on the fact that multiple independent predictions all came true, strengthening the argument for prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما المستقبلة: فمنها ما في القرآن: كقوله تعالى: {وَعَدَكُمُ اللهُ مَغَانِمَ كَثِيرَةً تَأْخُذُونَهَا} [الفتح: 20]، {الم * غُلِبَتِ الرُّومُ * فِي أَدْنَى الْأَرْضِ...} إلى قوله: {وَعْدَ اللَّهِ لَا يُخْلِفُ اللَّهُ وَعْدَهُ} [الروم: 1-6]، {سَنُلْقِي فِي قُلُوبِ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا الرَّعْبَ} [آل عمران: 151]، {سَيُهْزَمُ الْجَمْعُ وَيُوَلُّونَ الدُّبُرَ} [القمر: 45]، {سَتُدْعَوْنَ إِلَى قَوْمٍ أُولِي بَأْسٍ شَدِيدٍ} [الفتح: 16]، {لَيَسْتَخْلِفَنَّهُمْ فِي الْأَرْضِ} [النور: 55]، {لَتَدْخُلُنَّ الْمَسْجِدَ الْحَرَامَ} [الفتح: 27]، {لِيُظْهِرَهُ عَلَى الدِّينِ كُلِّهِ} [التوبة: 33]، {لَا يَأْتُونَ بِمِثْلِهِ} [الإسراء: 88]، {فَإِن لَّمْ تَفْعَلُوا وَلَن تَفْعَلُوا} [البقرة: 24]، {إِنَّ الَّذِي فَرَضَ عَلَيْكَ الْقُرْآنَ لَرَادُّكَ إِلَى مَعَادٍ} [القصص: 85]. ومنها ما ليس في القرآن: كقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام لعلي رضي الله تعالى عنه: «تُقَاتِلُ بَعْدِي النَّاكِثِينَ وَالْقَاسِطِينَ وَالْمَارِقِينَ»؛ ففيه الإخبار بالغيب من وجهين.
And as for the future: among them are those in the Quran, such as His saying the Exalted: {Allah has promised you much booty that you will take} [al-Fath: 20]; {Alif Lam Mim. The Romans have been defeated in the nearest land...} until His saying: {The promise of Allah; Allah does not break His promise} [al-Rum: 1-6]; {We will cast terror into the hearts of those who disbelieve} [Aal 'Imran: 151]; {The assembly will be defeated and they will turn their backs} [al-Qamar: 45]; {You will be called to a people of severe might} [al-Fath: 16]; {He will surely grant them succession in the land} [al-Nur: 55]; {You will surely enter the Sacred Mosque} [al-Fath: 27]; {That He may make it prevail over all religion} [al-Tawbah: 33]; {They will not bring the like of it} [al-Isra': 88]; {And if you do not – and you will never do it} [al-Baqarah: 24]; {Indeed, He who imposed the Quran upon you will return you to a place of return} [al-Qasas: 85]. And among them are those not in the Quran, such as his saying, peace and blessings be upon him, to Ali, may God be pleased with him: 'You will fight after me the breakers of the covenant, the deviators, and the renegades'; in it is the informing of the unseen in two respects.
Source pages p. 480

Commentary
This passage continues the classification of the second type of miracles: prophecies of future unseen events. Sanusi divides them into two categories: those mentioned in the Quran and those not in the Quran. For the Quranic ones, he lists multiple verses that contain clear predictions: (1) promise of abundant booty (al-Fath 20); (2) defeat of the Romans followed by victory (al-Rum 1-6); (3) terror cast into hearts of disbelievers (Aal 'Imran 151); (4) defeat of the enemy army (al-Qamar 45); (5) calling to fight a fierce people (al-Fath 16); (6) establishment of successors in the land (al-Nur 55); (7) entry into the Sacred Mosque (al-Fath 27); (8) prevailing of the religion (al-Tawbah 33); (9) inability to produce the like of the Quran (al-Isra' 88); (10) the threat that they will never do it (al-Baqarah 24); (11) return to Makkah (al-Qasas 85). All these were fulfilled. For non-Quranic predictions, he gives the hadith to Ali that he would fight three groups: the breakers of the covenant (the people of the Camel), the deviators (Muawiyah's party), and the renegades (the Kharijites). Sanusi notes that this hadith contains informing of the unseen in two respects (that Ali would fight after the Prophet's death, and that these specific groups would appear).

Key Terms
الغيوب المستقبلة
الإخبار بالغيب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think these verses are not predictions but general statements.
Correction: Sanusi treats them as specific prophecies that were historically fulfilled, as affirmed by the consensus of scholars.

Checkpoint
Which of the following verses does Sanusi cite as a prophecy of future events?
A) {Allah has promised you much booty that you will take} [al-Fath: 20]
B) {Indeed, Allah commands you to render trusts} [al-Nisa': 58]
C) {Say, He is Allah, the One} [al-Ikhlas: 1]
D) {The Most Merciful, established over the Throne} [Taha: 5]

Key Takeaway
Sanusi adduces eleven Quranic passages as evidence of the Prophet's miraculous foreknowledge of the future.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read these eleven predictions and reflect that every single one was fulfilled exactly as stated, does your heart truly accept that this Quran is from Allah, or are there doubts that you have been avoiding? What will you do today to strengthen your certainty in the Quran as divine word?
?
The verse 'And if you do not – and you will never do it' (al-Baqarah:24) is a challenge that remains unanswered. Have you ever truly pondered the implication that no human can produce even one chapter like the Quran? How does this challenge affect your personal relationship with the Quran?
?
Sanusi uses these prophecies as proof of prophethood. If someone were to ask you to present this evidence, would you be able to do so convincingly from your own understanding? What steps will you take to internalize this proof so it becomes part of your iman?

The Hadith of Ali as a Future Prophecy
Sanusi cites a hadith predicting Ali's future battles as a non-Quranic future prophecy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's hadith to Ali about fighting three groups constitutes a miracle of foretelling the unseen.

Core Idea
The Prophet predicted Ali's future battles with three specific groups—a prophecy that was precisely fulfilled.

Having presented Quranic prophecies, Sanusi now gives an example from the Prophetic hadith. He narrates the well-known tradition in which the Prophet told Ali that he would fight three groups after his death. Sanusi highlights that this prediction involves two distinct aspects of unseen knowledge, both of which came true exactly as foretold.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith text
Read the Arabic and translation of the hadith carefully, noting the specific details.
The hadith is short but contains two key elements.
2
Identify the two aspects
Sanusi says the hadith contains information about the unseen from two angles. Try to identify them before reading the commentary.
Think about what exactly was predicted.
3
Verify historical fulfillment
Research the historical events: Ali fought the people of the Camel (breakers of covenant), Muawiyah's forces (deviators), and the Kharijites (renegades).

And as for the future: among them are those in the Quran, such as His saying the Exalted: {Allah has promised you much booty that you will take} [al-Fath: 20]; {Alif Lam Mim. How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
This hadith reveals that even conflict among the Prophet's companions was part of divine decree. When you hear about divisions in the Muslim community today, do you respond with despair or with trust that God's plan is unfolding? How can this prophecy teach you to respond to internal strife with hope and patience?

Proofs of Prophethood through Foretelling the Unseen
Sanusi lists prophetic prophecies and explains the condition of da'wa al-nubuwwa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the fulfilled prophecies in the Quran and hadith, combined with the Prophet's claim of prophethood, serve as decisive proofs of Muhammad's prophethood.

Core Idea
Fulfilled prophecies plus the claim of prophethood equals undeniable proof.

Sanusi presents a compelling argument for prophethood by citing numerous prophecies from the Quran and hadith that were fulfilled exactly as foretold. He then explains the critical condition that these prophecies were accompanied by the claim of prophethood, which distinguishes them from miracles of saints or soothsayers and establishes them as true prophetic miracles.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic prophecies
Read the list of Quranic verses that contain prophecies. Notice how each one foretells a specific future event. These are part of the proof.
The verses are quoted with their chapter and verse numbers.
2
Examine the hadith prophecies
Read the hadith examples that also foretell future events. Pay attention to the prophecy about Ali and the others. Note that these are not in the Quran.
The hadith about Ali has two aspects of foretelling, as explained in the footnote.
3
Understand the condition of prophethood claim
Sanusi concludes that all these prophecies were accompanied by the claim of prophethood. This is what makes them miracles of prophethood, not just saintly miracles or soothsaying.
The claim of prophethood is the key distinguishing factor.
4
Distinguish prophetic miracles from others
Reflect on how the combination of foretelling the unseen with the claim of prophethood sets prophetic miracles apart from karamat (saint miracles) and irhasat (pre-prophethood signs).
This distinction is crucial for establishing prophethood.

We will cast terror into the hearts of those who disbelieve [Al-Imran 3:151]. The assembly will be defeated and they will turn their backs [Al-Qamar 54:45]. You will be called to a people of severe might [Al-Fath 48:16]. He will surely make them successors in the land [An-Nur 24:55]. You will surely enter the Sacred Mosque [Al-Fath 48:27]. He will make it prevail over all religion [At-Tawbah 9:33]. They cannot produce its like [Al-Isra 17:88]. If you do not do so – and you will never do so [Al-Baqarah 2:24]. Indeed, He who imposed the Quran upon you will surely bring you back to a place of return [Al-Qasas 28:85]. And among them are what is not in the Quran: like his saying, peace and blessings be upon him, to Ali, may God be pleased with him: 'You will fight after me the breakers of covenants, the oppressors, and the deviators.' That contains foretelling of the unseen in two aspects. After their defeat they will overcome in a few years – to God belongs the command before and after – and on that day the believers will rejoice in the victory of God; He gives victory to whom He wills, and He is the Mighty, the Merciful. [This is] the promise of God – God does not break His promise – but most people do not know [Ar-Rum 30:1-6]. (2) Rather, in three aspects, the third being the emergence of the breakers of covenants against him; and it may be said: it is derived from his fighting and entailed by it, so it is not considered an independent matter. Commentary
This passage is a compilation of proofs for prophethood through the foretelling of the unseen (ikbar bil-ghayb). The author first lists several Quranic verses that contain prophecies about future events: the casting of terror into the hearts of disbelievers (3:151), the defeat of the assembly (54:45), the call to a people of severe might (48:16), the succession in the land (24:55), the entry into the Sacred Mosque (48:27), the prevalence of the religion (9:33), the inability to produce the like of the Quran (17:88), the challenge to produce a sura (2:24), and the return to Makka (28:85). These are clear examples of prophecies in the Quran. Then the author says: 'And among them are what is not in the Quran' – meaning prophecies reported in hadith. The first example is the Prophet's statement to Ali: 'You will fight after me the breakers of covenants, the oppressors, and the deviators.' This contains two aspects of foretelling: the prior death of the Prophet and what was mentioned of Ali's fighting. The author then adds a footnote (2) noting that actually there are three aspects, the third being the emergence of the breakers of covenants against Ali. Further examples include: the prophecy that Ammar would be killed by the rebellious group; the folding of the earth for the Prophet and that his community's dominion would reach what was folded; the caliphate lasting thirty years after him; the destruction of Kisra and Caesar, the removal of their kingdom, and the spending of their treasures in God's path; and the domination of the Turks. The author notes that these prophecies are very many. The passage concludes with a critical point: all these prophecies were accompanied by the claim of prophethood (da'wa al-nubuwwa). This distinguishes them from karamat (miracles of saints) and irhasat (miracles before prophethood). Additionally, they are distinguished by purity of hearts and righteous deeds, and leaving revision (tark al-muraja'a – perhaps meaning not going back on the claim). Thus, the combination of foretelling the unseen with the claim of prophethood and other conditions provides a decisive proof of prophethood.

كرامة
إرهاصات

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that any foretelling of the future, even from a saint or soothsayer, proves prophethood.
Correction: The passage shows that the claim of prophethood and other conditions are necessary for it to be a miracle (mu'jiza) of a prophet.

Checkpoint
What distinguishes a prophetic miracle (mu'jiza) from a saint's miracle (karama) according to this passage?
A) The magnitude of the miracle
B) The presence of the claim of prophethood
C) The use of Quranic verses
D) The number of prophecies

Key Takeaway
The combination of fulfilled prophecies with the claim of prophethood provides an irrefutable proof of Muhammad's prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet foretold that Ali would fight certain groups after him, and it happened. In your life, do you treat every prophetic saying as surely true, or do you pick and choose? What is one hadith you have been avoiding acting upon? Will you commit to implementing it this week, no excuses?
?
The passage emphasizes that the prophecies were accompanied by the claim of prophethood. How does that challenge you to view every command of the Prophet as binding, not just spiritual advice? What is one area of your life—your work, your speech, your worship—where you have treated a prophetic instruction as optional? What will you change today?
?
If all these prophecies were fulfilled with such precision, what does that say about the Day of Judgment and the final return to Allah? Are you living as if that day is certain, or are you distracted by the immediate world? What is one concrete step you will take today to prepare for that meeting?

The Second Type of Miracles: Evidences and Distinction
Sanusi lists evidences of the second type of miracles and distinguishes them from karamat, irhasat, and sorcery.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the specific evidences for the second type of prophetic miracles and how they are distinguished from other supernatural events like saintly miracles and sorcery.

Core Idea
Prophetic miracles are distinguished by their association with the claim of prophethood and the prophet's purity.

This passage builds on the classification of miracles by presenting concrete examples from the Prophet's life and hadith. Sanusi lists several miraculous events and then clarifies how they are unique to prophethood, setting them apart from saintly miracles and sorcery.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the two main evidentiary points
The passage begins with 'One of them: the precedence of his death... and the second: what was mentioned of his fighting.' Note these two.
The hadiths that follow are supporting examples.
2
Examine the cited hadiths and understand their miraculous nature
Each hadith refers to a future event or hidden knowledge, which are signs of prophethood. Look at the content: the prophecy about Ammar, the folding of the earth, the caliphate duration, and the fall of empires.
These are prophecies that came true.
3
Learn how these miracles are distinguished from karamat and irhasat
The key is that they are associated with the claim of prophethood (دعوى النبوة). This is what separates them from saintly miracles or harbingers.
Saintly miracles are for saints not claiming prophethood; harbingers occur before prophethood.
4
Understand the distinction from sorcery and soothsaying
The passage states that the Prophet's purity of heart and righteous deeds, and his avoidance of astrology, distinguish his miracles from sorcery.
Sorcery relies on impure acts or celestial observations.

أحدهما : تقدُّمُ موتِهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ والثاني : ما ذكر مِنْ قتالِهِ وقولِهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ لعمَّارٍ رضيَ اللهُ تعالى عنه : « تَقْتُلُكَ الْفِئَةُ الْبَاغِيَةُ » وقوله عليه الصلاةُ والسلامُ : « زُوِيَتْ لِيَ الْأَرْضِ ، فَرَأَيْتُ مَشَارِقَهَا وَمَغَارِبَهَا ، وَسَيَبْلُغُ مُلْكُ أُمَّتِي مَا زُوِيَ لِي مِنْهَا » وقوله صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ : « الْخِلافَةُ بَعْدِي ثَلاثُونَ سَنَةً » وكإخباره بهلاكِ كسرى وقيصر ، وزوال ملكهما ، وإنفاق كنوزهما في سبيل الله تعالى ، وباستيلاء الأتراك ، إلى غير ذلكَ ممَّا ورد في الأحاديثِ ، وهو كثير جداً . وقد اقترنَ جميع ذلك بدعوى النبوَّةِ ; فيتميَّرُ عن الكرامة والإرهاصاتِ ، وبطهارة القلوبِ وصوالح الأعمال ، وتَرْكِ المراجعة إلى أحوال الكواكب والنظر في آلاتِها ; فيتميَّزُ عن السحر والكهانة وأمثال ذلكَ
One of them: the precedence of his death, peace be upon him, and the second: what was mentioned of his fighting. And his saying, peace be upon him, to Ammar, may Allah be pleased with him: 'The rebellious group will kill you.' And his saying, peace be upon him: 'The earth was folded for me, so I saw its easts and wests, and the dominion of my community will reach what was folded for me of it.' And his saying, peace be upon him: 'The caliphate after me is thirty years.' And like his informing of the destruction of Chosroes and Caesar, and the removal of their kingdom, and the spending of their treasures in the path of Allah, and the dominance of the Turks, and other things of that kind that occurred in the hadiths, and it is very abundant. And all of that was associated with the claim of prophethood, so it is distinguished from saintly miracles (karāmah) and harbingers (irhāṣāt), and by the purity of hearts and righteous deeds, and the abandonment of reference to the states of the planets and the examination of their instruments; so it is distinguished from sorcery (siḥr) and soothsaying (kihānah) and the like of that.
Source pages p. 482

Commentary
This passage presents the second type of prophetic miracles, listing several evidences from hadith. It begins by mentioning two specific things: the precedence of the Prophet's death and his fighting. Then it quotes hadiths: the hadith about Ammar being killed by the rebellious group, the hadith about the earth being folded for the Prophet and the future expansion of his community's rule, the hadith that the caliphate after him will be thirty years, and the prophecy of the destruction of the Persian and Roman empires and the dominance of the Turks. All these are abundant reports. The passage then explains that these events were all associated with his claim of prophethood (دعوى النبوة). This association distinguishes them from mere saintly miracles (كرامة) and prophetic precursors (إرهاصات) because they are directly tied to the prophetic claim. Additionally, they are distinguished from sorcery (سحر) and soothsaying (كهانة) by the purity of the Prophet's heart and his righteous deeds, and by the fact that the Prophet did not rely on astrology or examination of celestial bodies. Thus, these miracles are authentic proofs of his prophethood.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophetic miracles are the same as saintly miracles or sorcery.
Correction: Prophetic miracles are distinguished by being associated with the claim of prophethood and by the prophet's purity and avoidance of astrology.

Checkpoint

D) They are reported in many hadiths.

Key Takeaway
The second type of prophetic miracles are confirmed by multiple prophecies and are uniquely tied to the prophetic claim, setting them apart from other supernatural occurrences.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Examine your own life: When you hear of miraculous claims today, do you examine the character of the claimant as carefully as this lesson demands? Will you commit to seeking truth by looking at the whole picture—both the miracle and the moral character of the teacher?
?
The Prophet foretold events that came true—like the death of Chosroes and the thirty-year caliphate. Do you live as though these specific prophecies are mere stories, or do they compel you to submit to his authority in every area of your life? What is one practical change you can make today because you believe he knew the future?

This lesson shows that the prophet's rejection of astrology and his righteous deeds proved his miracles. What does your own lifestyle say about the source of your spiritual experiences?

Extraordinary Actions of the Prophet: Categories and Examples
Sanusi enumerates the third type of miracles and provides examples from essence and attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third type of the Prophet's miracles (extraordinary actions) and how they are categorized temporally and by subject, with examples from his essence and attributes.

Core Idea
Prophetic miracles include both physical wonders and moral perfections beyond human capacity.

Sanusi now turns to the third type of miracles: extraordinary actions that appeared through the Prophet. He emphasizes that these miracles are countless and categorizes them in two ways—temporally (before and after his claim to prophethood) and by subject (essence, attributes, and external matters). This lesson will walk through these divisions and highlight some of the astonishing examples from the Prophet's very being and character.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish from sorcery and note the vast number
Sanusi first distinguishes these miracles from sorcery and divination, then states they number over ten thousand. Reflect on the sheer abundance of prophetic miracles.
The count emphasizes that none knows them fully except Allah.
2
Learn the two temporal categories
The miracles are divided into preparatory (irhāṣiyyah) that occurred before his claim to prophethood, and confirmatory (taṣdīqiyyah) after.
This shows that even before his mission, Allah prepared signs.
3
Understand the three subject-based categories
Miracles are further divided into matters fixed in his essence (physical wonders), matters related to his attributes (moral perfections), and matters external to both (not detailed here).
The third category is mentioned but not expanded in this passage.
4
Examine examples from his essence (physical wonders)
Read the examples: the light passed through his forefathers, his birth circumcised, the seal of prophethood, his height changing, and seeing behind him as in front.
These are tangible signs in his very body.
5
Examine examples from his attributes (moral perfections)
Read the examples: his perfect truthfulness, trustworthiness (al-Amīn), chastity, unmatched bravery, eloquence, generosity, and asceticism.
These moral miracles are just as extraordinary as physical ones.

to the states of the planets and observation of their instruments; thus it is distinguished from sorcery, divination, and the like. The third type of his miracles, prayers and peace be upon him: many actions that appeared in him, or from his hand, or because of him, prayers and peace be upon him, contrary to custom: they number over a thousand, indeed over ten thousand, which none knows except Allah Almighty. Some of them were preparatory (irhāṣiyyah) appearing before the claim of prophethood, and some were confirmatory (taṣdīqiyyah) appearing after it. And they are divided into: matters fixed in his essence, matters related to his attributes, and matters external to both. As for the first: such as the light that was transmitted in his forefathers until he was born, and his birth circumcised and with his umbilical cord cut, raising his eyes, prayers and peace be upon him, to the heaven. And among the wonders of his essence, prayers and peace be upon him: the seal of prophethood that was between his shoulders, and the height of his stature, prayers and peace be upon him, when a tall person stood with him or walked with him, so that he, prayers and peace be upon him, became taller than that tall person, and his stature would equalize when he was alone or with a short or medium person, and his seeing behind him, prayers and peace be upon him, as he sees in front of him, and other such wonders of his essence that break custom. As for the second category — that which pertains to his attributes: matters without limit; among them: his attainment of the utmost degree of truthfulness such that not a single lie was ever recorded from him, prayers and peace be upon him, from the time he came into being; and trustworthiness such that he was called al-Amīn; and chastity and bravery such that not a single instance of retreating to flight was ever recorded from him, prayers and peace be upon him, even in the most difficult and severe battles like Hunayn and Uḥud; and eloquence and generosity whose extent cannot be encompassed; and asceticism in
Source pages p. 483

Commentary
This passage classifies the third type of the Prophet's miracles – extraordinary actions – and provides examples. The author first distinguishes these miracles from sorcery and similar practices, then states that these actions are countless, numbering in the thousands. He divides them into two temporal categories: some occurred before his claim to prophethood (irhāṣiyyah, preparatory miracles) and others after (taṣdīqiyyah, confirmatory). He then provides a threefold division based on subject: matters fixed in his essence (physical wonders), matters related to his attributes (moral perfections), and matters external to both (not detailed here). As examples of the first division, he mentions the light that passed through his forefathers, his birth already circumcised with his umbilical cord cut, his height changing to be taller when with a tall person, and his ability to see behind him as in front. For the second division, he lists his perfect truthfulness (never telling a lie), his trustworthiness (called al-Amīn), his chastity, his unmatched bravery (never fleeing from battle), his eloquence and generosity, and his asceticism. The passage emphasizes that these miracles are numerous and diverse, proving his prophethood through both physical and moral wonders.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think prophetic miracles are only external events like splitting the moon, but this passage shows that personal physical and moral attributes are also miraculous.
Correction: The Prophet's very essence and character were extraordinary, proving his prophethood through both physical wonders and moral perfections.

Checkpoint
Into how many categories does Sanusi divide the third type of miracles (extraordinary actions) by subject?
A) Two categories: preparatory and confirmatory
B) Three categories: essence, attributes, and external
C) Three categories: physical, moral, and spiritual
D) Two categories: personal and external

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's miracles include countless extraordinary actions in his essence and attributes, demonstrating that his very being and character were divinely exceptional.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet never told a single lie, from the moment he came into being. Where in your daily interactions do you find yourself compromising on truthfulness? What specific step will you take today to align your speech with his example?
?
The Prophet's bravery was so complete that he never retreated from battle, even at Hunayn and Uhud. When fear of failure or criticism tempts you to abandon what is right, whose example will you follow? What is one situation this week where you can stand firm like him?
?
The Prophet's attributes were miraculous gifts from Allah. Which of his qualities—truthfulness, trustworthiness, chastity, bravery, generosity—do you lack most? What practical change will you make this week to grow in that attribute?

Three Miraculous Signs of the Prophet's Body
Sanusi enumerates three miraculous physical attributes of the Prophet.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand three specific physical miracles of the Prophet that serve as signs of his prophethood and break the natural order.

Core Idea
The Prophet's body itself bore miraculous signs testifying to his prophethood.

In this lesson, we examine a passage from Sanusi's work on creed where he lists three extraordinary physical attributes of the Prophet Muhammad. These miracles are not merely symbolic; they are reported as literal events that defy normal human limitations. Understanding these wonders deepens our appreciation of the Prophet's unique status.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice how Sanusi introduces the topic and lists each miracle.
Pay attention to the numbers (1) and (2) in the Arabic text.
2
Identify the three miracles
List each miracle: the seal of prophethood, the variable height, and the ability to see behind. Note the specific description for each.
The third miracle is about vision, not blindness.
3
Consider the theological purpose
Think about why these physical miracles matter. They are not just wonders but confirmations of prophethood, showing that the Prophet's very being is extraordinary.
Sanusi concludes by saying these are among many wonders.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن عجائب ذاتِهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ : خاتم النبوَّةِ الذي كانَ لهُ بين كتفيه (١) ، وطول قامتِهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ إذا وقفَ معَهُ الطويل ، أو ماشاه حتى يكون هو صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ أطولَ مِنْ ذلكَ الطويل وتوشُطُ قامتِهِ إذا كانَ وحدَهُ أو مع القصير أو الوسط (۲) ، ورؤيتُهُ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ مَنْ خلفَهُ كما يرى مَنْ قَدَّامَهُ إِلى غيرِ ذلكَ مِنْ عجائب ذاتِهِ الخارقة للعادة
Among the wonders of his self, may Allah bless him and grant him peace: the seal of prophethood that was between his shoulders (1), and the height of his stature, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, when a tall person stood with him, or walked with him, until he, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, was taller than that tall person, and his stature would be average when he was alone or with a short or medium-sized person (2), and his seeing, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, those behind him as he sees those in front of him, and other such wonders of his self that break the usual course of things.
Source pages p. 484

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of miraculous physical attributes (khawāriq al-‘ādah) specific to the Prophet. The author lists three examples: first, the 'seal of prophethood' (khātam al-nubuwwa), a physical mark between his shoulders known from hadith. Second, his stature would miraculously adjust so that he appeared taller than any tall person standing with him, yet when alone or with shorter persons, he appeared of average height. Third, he could see people behind him just as clearly as those in front, a miracle of vision. The author concludes by noting that these are but a few of the many wonders of his physical nature that transcend normal human capability, thereby establishing the Prophet's unique physical constitution as a sign of his prophethood.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Thinking these miracles are symbolic or allegorical rather than literal occurrences.
Correction: The passage presents them as literal events (khawāriq al-‘ādah) that actually happened, breaking the normal course of nature.

Checkpoint

A) The seal of prophethood between his shoulders
B) His variable height when with tall or short people
C) His ability to see behind him as in front
D) His shadow being visible at all times

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's physical body exhibited miraculous traits that break the natural order, confirming his prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
These physical miracles of the Prophet were tangible signs of his prophethood. How often do you reflect on the physical reality of the Prophet's life as a proof of his message? Are you more moved by his words or by the miracles that accompanied him? Which of these three miracles stirs your heart most, and why?
?
The Prophet's variable stature is a miracle that changes how he appears depending on context. In your own life, do you seek to adjust your presence and character to benefit others, as the Prophet did physically? Or do you insist on a fixed image regardless of those around you?
?
Consider the miracle of seeing behind him. The Prophet had awareness beyond normal sight. How does this challenge your own limited perspective? Do you ignore the unseen realities of faith (like the Hereafter) because they are 'behind' you? What would change if you lived with the awareness that the Prophet's vision is a reminder of a greater reality?

The Prophet's Moral Perfection: Truthfulness, Trustworthiness, and Courage
Sanusi lists truthfulness, trustworthiness, chastity, and courage as moral miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key moral attributes of the Prophet Muhammad (ṣiddīq, amīn, shujāʿ) as rational miracles and how they are documented.

Core Idea
The Prophet's moral perfection is an evidence of his prophethood.

Sanusi begins the second category of miracles by focusing on the Prophet's personal attributes. These are not merely commendable traits; they are extraordinary (khāriq lil-ʿāda) because they reached a degree unattainable by humans. Let's examine the first set: truthfulness, trustworthiness, chastity, and courage.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about truthfulness and trustworthiness
Read the first part of the Arabic passage (from 'استجماعهُ' to 'الأمينَ') and its translation. Note that the Prophet never told a lie and was called al-Amīn.
This is a claim of historical fact, not just piety.
2
Understand courage and chastity
Read the part about 'العفاف والشجاعة' and the examples of Hunayn and Uhud. The Prophet never fled, even in the hardest battles.
This is a miracle because human nature inclines to flight in extreme danger.
3
Reflect on the miraculous nature
Ask yourself: Why are these considered miracles? Because they are beyond normal human capacity and serve as proofs of prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأمَّا القسم الثاني - وهو ما يرجعُ إلى صفاتِهِ - : فأمورٌ لا حصر منها : استجماعُهُ الغاية القصوى مِنَ الصدقِ حتى لم يُحفَظ لهُ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ قطُّ كَذبةٌ مِنْ حينَ وُجِد ، والأمانة حتى كانَ يُسمَّى الأمينَ ، والعفاف والشجاعة حتى لم تُحفَظْ عنهُ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ قط زحزحة إلى الفِرارِ ، ولو في أصعب الحروب وأشدها ؛ كحُنينٍ وأُحد (۳) ، والفصاحة والسماحة التي لا يُحاط بقدرها ، والزهد في الدنيا بأسرها ، والإيثار بعد التمكن منها . بل قد عُرِضَ عليه بالوحي أن يكون نبياً عبداً أو نبياً مَلِكاً ، فاختار أنْ يكونَ نبيّاً عبداً (۱) ، وعَرَضَ عليهِ جبريلُ أنْ تصيرَ لهُ جبالُ تهامة ذهباً تذهب معه حيثما ذهب ، وضمنَ لهُ معَ ذلكَ ألا ينقص له بسببٍ ذلكَ شيءٌ مِنْ رتبتِهِ التي هي فوق جميعِ الخلائقِ في الآخرة ، فقال : « يَا جِبْرِيلُ ؛ الدُّنْيَا دَارُ مَنْ لا دَارَ لَهُ ، وَيَسْعَى لَهَا مَنْ لا عَقْلَ لَهُ » ، واختار أن يجوع يوماً ويأكل يوماً ؛ ليتضرع ويشكر (٢) ومنها : التواضع لأهلِ المسكنة ، والشفقة على الأمة ، والمصابرة على متاعب الرسالة ، والمواظبة على مكارم الأخلاق ، وبلوغ النهاية في العلوم والمعارفِ الإلهيَّة ، وتمهيد المصالح الدينية والدنيوية . وفي يوم أُحُدٍ روى البخاري ( ۲۸۰٥ ) من حديث سيدنا أنس رضي الله عنه مرفوعاً : « اللهم ؛ إنِّي أعتذرُ إليكَ ممَّا صنع هؤلاء ـ يعني : أصحابه ـ وأبرأُ إليكَ ممَّا صنع هؤلاء ـ يعني : المشركين ـ » . وقد روى الترمذي ( ٢٣٤٧ ) من حديث سيدنا أبي أمامة رضي الله عنه مرفوعاً : عرض عليَّ ربِّي ليجعل لي بطحاء مكَّةَ ذهباً ، قلتُ : يا ربِّ ؛ ولكن أشبع يوماً وأجوعُ يوماً ؛ فإذا جُعتُ تضرّعتُ إليكَ وذكرتُكَ ، وإذا شبعت شكرتُكَ وحمدتكَ » . وروى أحمد في ( المسند » ( ٧١/٦ ) من حديث السيدة عائشة رضي الله عنها مرفوعاً : « الدنيا دارُ مَنْ لا دارَ لهُ ، ومالُ مَنْ لا مالَ لهُ ، ولها يجمعُ مَنْ لا عقل له » .
As for the second category – which pertains to his attributes – they are countless matters, among them: his attaining the ultimate degree of truthfulness, so that no lie was ever recorded from him, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, ever since he existed; and trustworthiness, so that he was called the Trustworthy (al-Amīn); and chastity and courage, so that no retreat to flight was ever recorded from him, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, even in the most difficult and severe battles, such as Hunayn and Uhud (3); and eloquence and generosity whose extent cannot be encompassed; and asceticism in the entire world; and preferring others even after being able to possess. Indeed, he was offered through revelation to be either a prophet-servant or a prophet-king, and he chose to be a prophet-servant (1). And Gabriel offered him that the mountains of Tihama become gold for him to take wherever he went, and he guaranteed him that nothing of his rank, which is above all creation in the Hereafter, would be diminished thereby; so he said: "O Gabriel, the world is the abode of one who has no abode, and he strives for it who has no intellect." And he chose to be hungry one day and to eat the next, so that he might supplicate and give thanks (2). And among them: humility towards the poor, compassion for the community, endurance of the hardships of the message, adherence to noble character, reaching the ultimate in divine sciences and knowledge, and establishing religious and worldly benefits. And on the day of Uhud, al-Bukhari narrated (2805) from the hadith of our master Anas, may Allah be pleased with him, raised to the Prophet: "O Allah, I apologize to You for what these (i.e., his companions) did, and I disassociate myself to You from what these (i.e., the polytheists) did." And al-Tirmidhi narrated (2347) from the hadith of our master Abu Umama, may Allah be pleased with him, raised to the Prophet: "My Lord offered me to make the plain of Mecca gold for me. I said: O Lord, but let me be full one day and hungry one day, so that when I am hungry I may supplicate to You and remember You, and when I am full I may thank You and praise You." And Ahmad narrated in al-Musnad (71/6) from the hadith of Lady Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her, raised to the Prophet: "The world is the abode of one who has no abode, and the wealth of one who has no wealth, and for it he collects who has no intellect."
Source pages p. 484

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration and illustration of the Prophet's moral and spiritual perfections. The author divides the miraculous into two categories: physical (covered earlier) and now the attributes of his character. He begins by listing several qualities: absolute truthfulness (sidq) such that no lie was ever recorded from him; trustworthiness (amāna) for which he was called al-Amīn; chastity and courage, with the proof that he never fled from battle even at Hunayn and Uhud; eloquence and generosity beyond measure; complete asceticism (zuhd) in this world; and selflessness (īthār) even after having means. Then he provides specific instances: the Prophet was given the choice to be a servant-prophet or a king-prophet, and he chose servanthood; Gabriel offered to turn the mountains of Tihama into gold for him without any loss of rank, but he refused, stating that the world is for those who have no real abode and no intellect; he chose to alternate between hunger and fullness to cultivate supplication and gratitude. The passage then lists additional qualities: humility, compassion, endurance, noble character, excellence in divine knowledge, and establishing religious and worldly benefits. Finally, the author cites three hadith: the Prophet's apology during Uhud disassociating from both his companions and the polytheists, the hadith of the offer of gold, and the saying that the world is for those without a true home.

أمانة
شجاعة
العفاف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think the Prophet's morality was ordinary or that he occasionally lied for strategic reasons.
Correction: The text asserts that no lie was ever recorded from him, and his trustworthiness was universally recognized, making it a miracle.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's perfect truthfulness, trustworthiness, and courage are miraculous proofs of his prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
After learning that the Prophet never told a single lie from the moment he existed, ask yourself: when was the last time I distorted the truth, even slightly? Am I willing to commit to absolute truthfulness starting today, no matter the cost? What is the first small lie I can eliminate from my life right now?
?
The Prophet was called al-Amin even before prophethood. In my own circle, am I known as trustworthy? Have I betrayed any trust—big or small—that I need to make amends for? Will I take concrete steps this week to restore that trust?
?
The Prophet never fled from battle, even when others did. What difficult situation am I currently running from—a difficult conversation, a duty I owe, a sin I need to confront? What would it look like for me to stand firm like the Prophet in that area starting now?

The Prophet's Asceticism and Selflessness: Choosing Servanthood over Kingship
Sanusi presents the Prophet's choice of servanthood and rejection of worldly wealth as miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Prophet's zuhd (asceticism) and ithar (selflessness) as demonstrated by his choice to be a servant-prophet and his refusal of worldly wealth.

Core Idea
The Prophet rejected worldly power and wealth for greater spiritual rank.

After enumerating basic moral virtues, Sanusi presents deeper spiritual miracles: the Prophet's complete detachment from this world and his preference for others. He was offered kingship and gold but chose servanthood and poverty. This lesson explores that choice and its significance.

Guided Path
1
Read about the choice between king-prophet and servant-prophet
Read the part where it says he was offered through revelation to be either a prophet-servant or a prophet-king. He chose the latter.
This is found in the source_arabic: 'بل قد عرض عليه بالوحي'.
2
Read Gabriel's offer of gold mountains
Read about the offer to turn the mountains of Tihama into gold. Note his reply: 'O Gabriel, the world is the abode of one who has no abode...'
This shows his complete disinterest in wealth.
3
Understand the pattern of hunger and fullness
Read his choice to alternate hunger and fullness to cultivate supplication and gratitude. This is the ultimate zuhd.

وأمَّا القسم الثاني - وهو ما يرجعُ إلى صفاتِهِ - : فأمورٌ لا حصر منها : استجماعُهُ الغاية القصوى مِنَ الصدقِ حتى لم يُحفَظ لهُ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ قطُّ كَذبةٌ مِنْ حينَ وُجِد ، والأمانة حتى كانَ يُسمَّى الأمينَ ، والعفاف والشجاعة حتى لم تُحفَظْ عنهُ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ قط زحزحة إلى الفِرارِ ، ولو في أصعب الحروب وأشدها ؛ كحُنينٍ وأُحد (۳) ، والفصاحة والسماحة التي لا يُحاط بقدرها ، والزهد في الدنيا بأسرها ، والإيثار بعد التمكن منها . بل قد عُرِضَ عليه بالوحي أن يكون نبياً عبداً أو نبياً مَلِكاً ، فاختار أنْ يكونَ نبيّاً عبداً (۱) ، وعَرَضَ عليهِ جبريلُ أنْ تصيرَ لهُ جبالُ تهامة ذهباً تذهب معه حيثما ذهب ، وضمنَ لهُ معَ ذلكَ ألا ينقص له بسببٍ ذلكَ شيءٌ مِنْ رتبتِهِ التي هي فوق جميعِ الخلائقِ في الآخرة ، فقال : « يَا جِبْرِيلُ ؛ الدُّنْيَا دَارُ مَنْ لا دَارَ لَهُ ، وَيَسْعَى لَهَا مَنْ لا عَقْلَ لَهُ » ، واختار أن يجوع يوماً ويأكل يوماً ؛ ليتضرع ويشكر (٢) ومنها : التواضع لأهلِ المسكنة ، والشفقة على الأمة ، والمصابرة على متاعب الرسالة ، والمواظبة على مكارم الأخلاق ، وبلوغ النهاية في العلوم والمعارفِ الإلهيَّة ، وتمهيد المصالح الدينية والدنيوية . وفي يوم أُحُدٍ روى البخاري ( ۲۸۰٥ ) من حديث سيدنا أنس رضي الله عنه مرفوعاً : « اللهم ؛ إنِّي أعتذرُ إليكَ ممَّا صنع هؤلاء ـ يعني : أصحابه ـ وأبرأُ إليكَ ممَّا صنع هؤلاء ـ يعني : المشركين ـ » . وقد روى الترمذي ( ٢٣٤٧ ) من حديث سيدنا أبي أمامة رضي الله عنه مرفوعاً : عرض عليَّ ربِّي ليجعل لي بطحاء مكَّةَ ذهباً ، قلتُ : يا ربِّ ؛ ولكن أشبع يوماً وأجوعُ يوماً ؛ فإذا جُعتُ تضرّعتُ إليكَ وذكرتُكَ ، وإذا شبعت شكرتُكَ وحمدتكَ » . وروى أحمد في ( المسند » ( ٧١/٦ ) من حديث السيدة عائشة رضي الله عنها مرفوعاً : « الدنيا دارُ مَنْ لا دارَ لهُ ، ومالُ مَنْ لا مالَ لهُ ، ولها يجمعُ مَنْ لا عقل له » .
As for the second category – which pertains to his attributes – they are countless matters, among them: his attaining the ultimate degree of truthfulness, so that no lie was ever recorded from him, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, ever since he existed; and trustworthiness, so that he was called the Trustworthy (al-Amīn); and chastity and courage, so that no retreat to flight was ever recorded from him, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, even in the most difficult and severe battles, such as Hunayn and Uhud (3); and eloquence and generosity whose extent cannot be encompassed; and asceticism in the entire world; and preferring others even after being able to possess. Indeed, he was offered through revelation to be either a prophet-servant or a prophet-king, and he chose to be a prophet-servant (1). And Gabriel offered him that the mountains of Tihama become gold for him to take wherever he went, and he guaranteed him that nothing of his rank, which is above all creation in the Hereafter, would be diminished thereby; so he said: "O Gabriel, the world is the abode of one who has no abode, and he strives for it who has no intellect." And he chose to be hungry one day and to eat the next, so that he might supplicate and give thanks (2). And among them: humility towards the poor, compassion for the community, endurance of the hardships of the message, adherence to noble character, reaching the ultimate in divine sciences and knowledge, and establishing religious and worldly benefits. And on the day of Uhud, al-Bukhari narrated (2805) from the hadith of our master Anas, may Allah be pleased with him, raised to the Prophet: "O Allah, I apologize to You for what these (i.e., his companions) did, and I disassociate myself to You from what these (i.e., the polytheists) did." And al-Tirmidhi narrated (2347) from the hadith of our master Abu Umama, may Allah be pleased with him, raised to the Prophet: "My Lord offered me to make the plain of Mecca gold for me. I said: O Lord, but let me be full one day and hungry one day, so that when I am hungry I may supplicate to You and remember You, and when I am full I may thank You and praise You." And Ahmad narrated in al-Musnad (71/6) from the hadith of Lady Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her, raised to the Prophet: "The world is the abode of one who has no abode, and the wealth of one who has no wealth, and for it he collects who has no intellect."
Source pages p. 484

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration and illustration of the Prophet's moral and spiritual perfections. The author divides the miraculous into two categories: physical (covered earlier) and now the attributes of his character. He begins by listing several qualities: absolute truthfulness (sidq) such that no lie was ever recorded from him; trustworthiness (amāna) for which he was called al-Amīn; chastity and courage, with the proof that he never fled from battle even at Hunayn and Uhud; eloquence and generosity beyond measure; complete asceticism (zuhd) in this world; and selflessness (īthār) even after having means. Then he provides specific instances: the Prophet was given the choice to be a servant-prophet or a king-prophet, and he chose servanthood; Gabriel offered to turn the mountains of Tihama into gold for him without any loss of rank, but he refused, stating that the world is for those who have no real abode and no intellect; he chose to alternate between hunger and fullness to cultivate supplication and gratitude. The passage then lists additional qualities: humility, compassion, endurance, noble character, excellence in divine knowledge, and establishing religious and worldly benefits. Finally, the author cites three hadith: the Prophet's apology during Uhud disassociating from both his companions and the polytheists, the hadith of the offer of gold, and the saying that the world is for those without a true home.

Key Terms
زهد
إيثار
عبودية
نبي عبد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the Prophet's rejection of wealth indicates that poverty is inherently good or that he was unable to attain wealth.
Correction: The text emphasizes he was offered wealth and power without any loss of rank, but he chose poverty out of humility and devotion, not inability.

Checkpoint
What did the Prophet say when Gabriel offered him gold mountains?
A) 'I am the king of kings'
B) 'The world is the abode of one who has no abode'
C) 'Give it to the poor'
D) 'I accept for my ummah'

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's choice of servanthood over kingship and refusal of gold demonstrate his miraculous asceticism and selflessness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you willing to give up a position of power or wealth to draw closer to Allah? What worldly achievement would be hardest for you to refuse if it came with a guarantee of preserving your faith?
?
The Prophet chose hunger and fullness alternately to remain in a state of supplication and gratitude. When was the last time you voluntarily experienced discomfort or deprivation to increase your devotion to Allah, not out of necessity but choice?
?
If you were offered a promotion or financial windfall with the assurance that your spiritual rank would not decrease, would you take it? Why did the Prophet refuse such an offer, and what does that reveal about your own attachment to the world?

Prophethood
intermediate
8 min
Comprehensive Virtues and Hadith Evidences
Sanusi lists further virtues and cites three hadiths as evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the comprehensive moral and spiritual virtues of the Prophet as listed by Sanusi, supported by three hadiths that illustrate his humility, compassion, and detachment.

Core Idea
The Prophet's character encompasses all noble traits, confirmed by authentic hadith.

Sanusi completes his enumeration with a list of additional virtues: humility, compassion, endurance, noble character, and knowledge. He then supports these with three hadiths: the Prophet's apology at Uhud, the offer of gold, and the statement about the world. Let's examine these to see how the Prophet's actions embody his teachings.

Guided Path
1
Read the list of additional virtues
Read from 'ومنها : التواضع...' to '...والدنيوية'. Note the qualities: humility, compassion, endurance, noble character, divine knowledge, and establishing benefits.
These are not just personal traits but also his role as a messenger.
2
Study the hadith on Uhud
Read the hadith where the Prophet apologizes to Allah for his companions and dissociates from the polytheists. This shows his compassion and fairness.
He intercedes even for those who disobeyed.
3
Study the hadith on the offer of gold (Tirmidhi version)
Read the variant hadith from Abu Umama where he says he wants to be hungry one day and full one day to supplicate and thank.
This reinforces his choice mentioned earlier.
4
Study the hadith about the world
Read the hadith from Ahmad: 'The world is the abode of one who has no abode...' Understand it as his conviction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the Prophet's apology at Uhud indicates he was wrong or his companions were all sinful.
Correction: The apology is an expression of his humility and role as intercessor, not an admission of guilt.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet endured the hardships of the message with patience. When you face difficulty in conveying the truth or standing for Islam, do you complain or retreat? What is one situation today where you can choose patience instead of frustration?
?
He chose hunger over wealth to increase his supplication and gratitude. Which comfort or luxury are you unwilling to give up for the sake of drawing closer to Allah? Will you take a concrete step to detach from it this week?
?
At Uhud, the Prophet apologized to Allah for his companions' mistakes. When someone wrongs you, do you hold a grudge or do you seek forgiveness for them? How can you practice that kind of compassion in your next interaction?

Prophethood
intermediate
5 min
Miraculous Signs at the Birth of the Prophet
Narrates the miraculous signs at the Prophet's birth and the consultation of the soothsayer Soteeh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the miraculous signs that accompanied the birth of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) and how they were interpreted by the Persian court as a sign of a new prophet.

Core Idea
The birth of the Prophet was marked by supernatural events recognized even by pagans.

In this passage, the Muslim scholar Sanusi narrates a series of extraordinary events that occurred at the moment of the Prophet Muhammad's birth. These signs—including the trembling of the Persian king's palace, the falling of battlements, the drying of a lake, and the extinguishing of sacred fires—were reported from various regions. The Persian king sought advice from a soothsayer, indicating that even non-Muslims perceived the significance of this birth. This lesson explores these signs as evidence of prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the description of the signs
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its translation. Pay attention to the specific events: the iwan trembling, the battlements falling, the lake drying, the fire temples extinguishing, and the river stopping.
These are not just natural phenomena; they are presented as supernatural confirmations.
2
Understand Kisra's reaction
Notice that the Persian king Kisra receives reports from different provinces and then consults a soothsayer. This shows that even the mighty empire was shaken by these events.
The soothsayer Satih is described in a strange way, emphasizing his supernatural knowledge.
3
Analyze the poem and its purpose
The poem recited by Abd al-Masih is a lamentation asking if Satih is dead or alive, and describing the messenger (the Prophet). Though the poem's words are obscure, its purpose is to confirm the news.
The glosses at the end explain some poetic terms like 'al-Ghatrif' meaning noble master.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أُخْتُ بَنِي زُهْرَةَ مِنْ سِرِّكُمْ فِي غَابِرِ الدَّهْرِ وَعِنْدَ الْبَدِي وَاحِدَةٌ مِنْكُمْ فَهَاتُوا لَنَا فِيمَا مَضَى لِلنَّاسِ أَوْ مَا بَقِي وَاحِدَةٌ مِنْ خَيْرِكُمْ مِثْلَهَا جَنِينُهَا مِثْلُ النَّبِيِّ التَّقِـي وارتعدَ عند ولادتِهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسَلَّمَ إِيوانُ كسرى أَنوشَرْوانَ بنِ قباد بن فيروز ، وسقطَتْ مِنْ قصرِهِ أربع عشرة شرافة ، وكتب إليهِ صاحب اليمن يخبرُهُ بأنَّ بحيرة ساوة غاضَتْ تلك الليلةَ ، وكتب إليهِ صاحبُ فارس يخبرُهُ بأنَّ بيوت النيران التي يعبدونها قد خمدَتْ تلك الليلةَ ، ولم تكن خمدَتْ قبلَ ذلكَ بألفِ سنةٍ ، وكتب إليه صاحبُ الشامِ يخبرُهُ بأنَّ وادي السماوة انقطعَتْ جَرْيتُهُ تلك الليلة ثم أخبرَهُ المُوبَذانُ - ومعناه : القاضي والمفتي بلغتهم - أنَّه رأى إبلاً صعاباً ، تقود خيلاً عِراباً ، فانتشرَتْ في بلادهم . فأرسل كسرى عبد المسيح الغساني إلى سطيح الكاهن - وكانَ مِنْ أخواله - يستخبرُهُ علم ذلكَ ، وكانَ سطيح جسداً ملقئ لا جوارح له ، ووجهه في صدرِهِ ، لم يكن له رأس ولا عنقٌ ، لا يقدر على الجلوس إلا إذا غضبَ انتفخَ ، وقد قيلَ لَهُ : أَنَّى لك هذا العلم ؟ فقال : لي صاحب مِنَ الجِنِّ استمعَ أخبار السماءِ مِنْ طُورِ سيناءَ حِينَ كلَّمَ اللهُ تعالى موسى عليه الصلاة والسلام ، فهو يؤدِّي إِليَّ مِنْ ذلكَ ما يؤدِّي فلما قدمَ عليهِ عبد المسيح وجدَهُ قد أشفى على الموتِ ، فسلَّمَ عليهِ ، فلم يرد عليه جواباً ، فأنشأ عبد المسيح يقول : [ من الرجز ] أَصُمَّ أَمْ يَسْمَعُ غِطْرِيفُ الْيَمَنْ أَمْ فَادَ فَازْلَـمَّ بِهِ شَأْوُ الْعَنَنْ يَا فَاضِلَ الْخُطْبَةِ أَعَيَتْ مَنْ وَمَنْ أَتَاكَ شَيْخُ الْحَيَّ مِنْ آلِ سَنَنْ وَأُمُّهُ مِنْ آلِ ذِنْبِ بْنِ حَجَنْ أَبْيَضُ فَضْفَاضُ الرَّدَاءِ وَالْبَدَنُ رَسُولُ قَيْلِ الْعُجْمِ يَسْرِي فِي الْوَسَنُ لا يَرْهَبُ الرَّعْدَ وَلا رَيْبَ الزَّمَنْ يَجُوبُ فِي الْأَرْضِ عَلَنْدَاةٌ شَرَنْ تَرْفَعُنِي وَجُناً وَتَهْوِي بِي وَجَنْ حَتَّى أَتَى عَارِي الْجَاجِي وَالْقَطَنْ [تَلَفهُ] فِي الرِّيح بَوْغَاءُ الدِّمَنْ الغطريف : السيد الشريف ، وفادَ يفودُ : ماتَ ، وازلم : قبضَ أو
The sister of Banu Zahra from your secret in the remainder of time and at the beginning, one of you. So bring to us, regarding what has passed for people or what remains, one of your best like her, her fetus like the pious Prophet. And at his birth, may God bless him and grant him peace, the iwan of Kisra Anushirwan ibn Qubad ibn Firuz trembled, and from his palace fourteen battlements fell. And the ruler of Yemen wrote to him informing him that the lake of Sawa had dried up that night. And the ruler of Persia wrote to him informing him that the fire temples which they worshipped had been extinguished that night, and they had not been extinguished for a thousand years before that. And the ruler of Syria wrote to him informing him that the valley of Samawa had ceased its flow that night. Then the Mobedhan – its meaning: the judge and mufti in their language – informed him that he saw difficult camels leading noble horses, and they spread throughout their lands. So Kisra sent Abd al-Masih al-Ghassani to Satih the soothsayer – and he was from his maternal uncles – to inquire from him the knowledge of that. And Satih was a thrown body with no limbs, his face in his chest, no head or neck, unable to sit unless he became angry and swelled. And it was said to him: How did you get this knowledge? He said: I have a companion from the jinn who listens to the news of the sky from Mount Sinai when God Almighty spoke to Moses, peace be upon him, and he conveys to me from that what he conveys. When Abd al-Masih came to him, he found him at the point of death. So he greeted him, but he did not return his greeting. So Abd al-Masih began to speak: [in rajaz meter] Is Ghatrif of Yemen deaf or does he hear? Or has he died and his worldly course been cut short? O excellent in speech, the two of you and others? A sheikh of the tribe coming from the family of Sanan, and his mother from the family of Dhanb ibn Hajan, white, with flowing garments and body. The messenger of the non-Arab governor travels in drowsiness, he fears not thunder nor the vicissitudes of time. He traverses the earth, a large swift she-camel, she lifts me and lowers me. Until I came to the bare one of the haj and qatan [؟tosses him?] in the wind, the dust of dung. al-Ghatrif: the noble master, and fada yafudu: he died, and izlam: he seized or
Source pages p. 487

Commentary
This passage is a historical narrative that reports the miraculous signs accompanying the birth of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him). It begins with an enigmatic phrase addressed to the Banu Zahra, then describes specific events: the trembling of the iwan (throne hall) of the Persian king Kisra, the falling of fourteen battlements from his palace, reports from Yemen about the drying of Lake Sawa, from Persia about the extinguishing of fire temples (which had burned for a thousand years), and from Syria about the stoppage of the river Samawa. Then the Mobedhan (the Zoroastrian high priest) reports a dream of difficult camels leading noble horses spreading in their land. Kisra then sends Abd al-Masih al-Ghassani to consult the soothsayer Satih, who is described as a deformed creature with no limbs, face in chest, no head or neck, who only sits when angry. When asked how he knows, Satih says a jinni brings him news from Mount Sinai where God spoke to Moses. Abd al-Masih finds Satih dying and recites a poem essentially asking if he is dead or alive, describing the messenger who has come (the Prophet). The poem contains obscurities. The passage ends with glosses on some poetic words: al-Ghatrif means noble master, fada yafudu means died, and izlam means seized. The narrative is presented as a proof of prophethood, showing that even the Persian monarchy and soothsayers recognized the significance of the birth.

Key Terms
إِيوان كسرى
بحيرة ساوة
سطيح الكاهن
الموبذان
غطريف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This story is a hadith (prophetic tradition) and must be accepted as authentic.
Correction: This narrative is not from the Prophet but is a historical report from earlier scholars. Its purpose is to show that even non-Muslims recognized the miraculous nature of the Prophet's birth.

Checkpoint

A) Twelve
B) Fourteen
C) Ten
D) Seven

Key Takeaway
The birth of the Prophet Muhammad was accompanied by multiple supernatural signs that were reported across the Persian Empire, confirming his prophethood even to non-Muslims.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Persians saw clear signs—a trembling palace, extinguished fires—yet they did not believe. What signs has Allah placed in your life that you have brushed aside? Will you wait for a 'greater' miracle before you submit fully?
?
Satih the soothsayer heard the truth from a jinn and still did not act. You have the Quran and the authentic sunna. What excuse will you bring on the Day of Judgment for failing to change?
?
The fire temples burned for a thousand years and were put out the night the Prophet was born. What old habits or sins have been burning in your heart for years? Is there a light of guidance ready to extinguish them today?

Sateeh's Prophecy of the Prophet's Coming
Sateeh predicts the Prophet's arrival through signs and portents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how pre-Islamic prophecies, such as that of Sateeh, serve as proofs of the prophethood of Muhammad (peace be upon him) by listing specific supernatural signs.

Core Idea
Prophecies of the Prophet's coming confirm his truth through signs and portents.

In this lesson, we will examine a famous prophecy attributed to the soothsayer Sateeh, which foretells the arrival of the final Prophet through a series of miraculous signs. This narrative is a classic proof of prophethood (دليل النبوة) in Islamic tradition. Let's read the passage and understand its significance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once through, then read the English translation. Let the rhythm of the narrative sink in before analyzing.
Notice the poetic style and the listing of signs.
2
Identify the supernatural signs
List all the signs mentioned: trembling of the arch, extinguishing of fires, the magus's dream, drying up of lake and valley, etc.
Some signs are past (already occurred), others are future.
3
Connect signs to the Prophet's mission
Understand that 'the recitation' refers to the Qur'an and 'the bearer of the club' refers to the sword of jihad, indicating the Prophet's arrival.
Sateeh explicitly links these signs to the coming of the final Prophet.
4
Recognize the proof structure
This passage is a type of miracle (prediction) used in Islamic theology to confirm the truth of Muhammad's prophethood.
Such prophecies are considered دلائل النبوة (proofs of prophethood).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلما سمع سطيح شعرَهُ رفع رأسَهُ وقالَ : عبد المسيح ، على جمل مشِيخ - أي : مسرع - ، جاءَ إلى سطيخ ، وقد أوفى على الضريح ، بني ساسان ، لارتجاس الإيوان ، وخمودِ النيران ، ورؤيا المُوبَذانِ ؛ رأى إبلاً صعابا ، تقود خيلاً عِرابا ، قد قطعت دجله ، وانتشرَتْ في بلادها • بعثك ملك عبد المسيح ؛ إذا كثرَتِ التلاوة ، وظهر صاحب الهراوة - يعني : السيف ـ ، وخمدَتْ نارُ فارس ، وغاضَتْ بحيرة ساوه ، وغاض وادي السماوة .. فليسَتِ الشامُ السطيح شاما ، يملك منهم ملوكاً وملكات على عددِ الشرافات ، وكلُّ ما هو آت آتْ
When Sateeh heard his poem, he raised his head and said: 'O Abdul Masih, upon a swift camel—meaning fast—you have come to Sateeh while he has approached the grave. The house of Sasan [is doomed] because of the trembling of the arch, the extinguishing of the fires, and the dream of the magus: he saw difficult camels leading excellent horses that had crossed the Tigris and spread in its lands. A king sent you, O Abdul Masih. When the recitation multiplies and the bearer of the club—meaning the sword—appears, and the fire of Persia is extinguished, and the lake of Sawa dries up, and the valley of Samawa dries up... Then it is not the Sham of Sateeh, it is Sham; they will have kings and queens among them equal to the number of the roofs. And all that is coming will come.'
Source pages p. 488

Commentary
This passage presents a proof of prophethood (دليل النبوة) through the prediction of Sateeh, a legendary soothsayer or monk, who foretells the coming of the final Prophet by interpreting supernatural signs. The narrative begins with Sateeh's response to Abdul Masih's poem, where he describes the signs that have already occurred (the trembling of the imperial arch of Kisra, the extinguishing of the Persian sacred fires, the dream of the magus seeing camels leading horses across the Tigris) as indicators of a great change. These events are historically linked to the period just before the birth or mission of Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him). Sateeh then declares that these signs herald the coming of one who will bring the 'recitation' (the Qur'an) and wield the 'sword' (jihad), and that the Persian empire will collapse. The drying up of Lake Sawa and the valley of Samawa are additional portents. The final statement, 'and all that is coming will come,' affirms the certainty of the prophecy. This is a classic example of how pre-Islamic predictions were used in Islamic tradition to confirm the truth of Muhammad's prophethood.

Key Terms
سطيح
نبوءة
دلائل النبوة
الهراوة
خمود النيران

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think this prophecy is a direct historical quote from a known figure.
Correction: This narrative is used in Islamic tradition as a proof of prophethood, not necessarily a verbatim historical record.

Checkpoint

A) The trembling of the arch, extinguishing of fires, and the dream of the magus
B) The appearance of a comet and an eclipse
C) The flooding of the Tigris and the birth of a white calf
D) The destruction of the Kaaba and the death of the Persian king

Key Takeaway
The prophecy of Sateeh, with its detailed signs, serves as a miraculous proof of the Prophet Muhammad's coming, affirming the truth of Islam.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read Sateeh's prophecy, do you truly feel the certainty that these signs confirm the truth of Islam? Or do you treat them as mere stories? If they are true, how should that change your urgency to obey the Prophet today?
?
The signs Sateeh listed were clear and undeniable. In your own life, what signs has Allah given you to confirm the truth? Are you ignoring them?
?
The passage ends with 'all that is coming will come.' Are you living as if you truly believe that everything Allah has promised—including the Day of Judgment—is coming without doubt? Or do you live as if it's far off?

The Prophecy of the Fall of the Persian Kingdom
Reports the fulfillment of the Prophet's supplication against Persia.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's supplication against the Persian empire was a historical sign of his prophethood, fulfilled through the Muslim conquest.

Core Idea
The Prophet's prayer to tear apart Persia was answered in history.

This passage from Sanusi's work presents a historical evidence for prophethood: the fulfillment of the Prophet's supplication against the Persian kingdom. It recounts the brief succession of Persian rulers after the death of a soothsayer and how the entire kingdom fell to the Muslims as a direct result of the Prophet's prayer. This demonstrates that his words were not ordinary but divinely backed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main claim
Read the passage and find the statement that directly attributes the end of the Persian kingdom to the Prophet's supplication.
Look for the phrase 'بدعائه صلى الله عليه وسلم'.
2
Understand the context
The passage mentions Satih and the count of Persian kings. Notice that this background shows the accuracy of the prophecy.
Satih was a soothsayer who predicted the end of Persian rule.
3
Connect to the concept of miracles
This event is presented as a mu'jiza (miracle) confirming prophethood. Reflect on why answered supplication is a sign.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم مات سطيح مكانه قالوا وكان أقصى ملكهم عشرة من الرجال وامرأتين فنقص عن عدد الشرافات اثنان ولعله أخطأ في النقل وقد انقضى ملكهم وقهرهم الإسلام وفتحت بلادهم على يد عمر بن الخطاب رضي الله تعالى عنه وذلك بدعائه صلى الله عليه وسلم أن يمزقوا كل ممزق فلم يكن للفرس ملك بعد
Then Satih died in his place. They said: The extent of their kingship was ten men and two women, so it fell short of the number of the honored ones (al-sharafat) by two, and perhaps he erred in transmission. And their kingship ended, and Islam overpowered them, and their lands were conquered at the hands of 'Umar ibn al-Khattab, may Allah be pleased with him; and that was by his supplication, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, that they be torn apart utterly. So there was no kingship for the Persians afterwards.
Source pages p. 490

Commentary
This passage reports a historical sign of prophecy: the fulfillment of the Prophet's supplication against the Persian empire. It begins by mentioning the death of the soothsayer Satih, then recounts the brief span of Persian kings after that, noting a discrepancy in the count. The key point is that the Persian kingdom was ended by the Muslims due to the Prophet's prayer that they be torn apart. This is presented as a miracle (mu'jiza) of the Prophet, showing that his supplications were answered.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This passage is only about the soothsayer Satih and the count of Persian kings.
Correction: The passage's main purpose is to show the fulfillment of the Prophet's supplication as a miracle.

?

Four Miracles of the Prophet
Enumerates four miracles: cloud, moon, stone, and tree.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the enumeration of four miraculous occurrences demonstrating the Prophet's prophethood.

Core Idea
Four miracles illustrate the Prophet's unique status.

This passage from Sanusi's text lists four remarkable events that signify the Prophet's prophethood. While miracles at birth are many, the author focuses on the cloud, moon, stone, and tree. Each event is a distinct sign from Allah. Let's explore them as presented.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Notice the flow from stating many wonders to listing four specific miracles.
The passage uses 'ومنها' (among them) to introduce each item.
2
Identify each miracle
Find the four miracles: cloud shading, moon splitting, stone greeting, and tree uprooting. Also note the tree's additional action of wrapping around the Prophet.
3
Understand the tree's miracle
The tree not only came and greeted the Prophet but also wrapped around him for privacy. The author notes this is authenticated.
This shows the miraculous responsiveness of creation.
4
Reflect on the purpose
Ask: Why are these miracles mentioned? They affirm prophethood and show Allah's power over nature.
They are clear signs for those who reflect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد عد من العجائب التي كانت عند ولادته عليه الصلاة والسلام أمور كثيرة يطول ذكرها ومنها إظلال السحاب عليه صلى الله عليه وسلم وانشقاق القمر وتسليم الحجر وانقلاع الشجرة ومجيئها تخط بعروقها الأرض حتى وقفت بين يديه وسلمت عليه وشهدت له صلى الله عليه وسلم بالنبوة ورجعت إلى مكانها وقد صح مجيئها أيضا والتفافها عليه لقضاء حاجته صلى الله عليه وسلم في مواطن
And among the wondrous things that existed at his birth, peace and blessings be upon him, are many matters too lengthy to mention. Among them: the cloud shading him, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and the splitting of the moon, and the stone's greeting, and the tree uprooting itself and coming, plowing the earth with its roots until it stood before him, and it greeted him and testified to his prophethood, and returned to its place; and its coming also has been authenticated, and its wrapping around him to accommodate his need, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, in certain places.
Source pages p. 490

Commentary
This passage enumerates several miracles associated with the Prophet. It begins by stating that there are many wonders at his birth. Then it lists: 1) a cloud shading him; 2) the splitting of the moon (a well-known miracle); 3) a stone greeting him; 4) a tree uprooting itself and coming to him, greeting him and testifying to his prophethood, then returning; additionally, it also wrapped around him for privacy. The author notes that the coming of the tree is authenticated. This is a brief compilation of multiple signs of prophethood.

Key Terms
إظلال السحاب
انشقاق القمر
تسليم الحجر
انقلاع الشجرة
معجزة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All these miracles happened at the exact moment of birth.
Correction: The passage says 'at his birth' but includes the moon splitting (which occurred later in Medina) and other events that may have occurred at different times. They are wonders associated with his life, not necessarily all at birth.

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

When you read these miracles, do you feel the same certainty, or has indifference crept in? Today, will you make a sincere dua asking Allah to increase your conviction in the Prophet's message?
?
The tree uprooted itself and traveled to serve the Prophet, even plowing the earth with its roots. What comfort zones or attachments are you unwilling to uproot for the sake of following the Prophet? Will you identify one habit this week that you will 'uproot'—even temporarily—to draw closer to his sunnah?

Food Multiplication Miracle
Describes the miracle of food multiplication.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the miracle of food multiplication as a proof of prophethood and the two means by which it occurred.

Core Idea
Food multiplication is a clear prophetic miracle.

This lesson presents another category of prophetic miracles: the blessing of food. The Prophet ﷺ could feed a large number of people from a small amount of food, either by his touch or his supplication, demonstrating Allah’s power through him. This miraculous multiplication is one of the well-known signs of prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic sentence slowly, noting the key terms for satiation and multiplication. This will help you connect the words to the concept.
2
Understand the two causes
The passage mentions two ways the miracle occurred: the Prophet placing his hand in the food, or his supplication. Reflect on how both are acts of the Prophet that channel divine power.
3
Recognize the miraculous nature
Feeding many with little food defies natural laws. This is a miracle (kharq al-‘adah) that confirms prophethood.
4
Connect to broader theme
This miracle is part of a series of evidences for prophethood. Think about how such events strengthen faith in the Prophet's mission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها شبع الخلق الكثير من طعامه اليسير وتكثيره بسبب وضع يده فيه أو دعائه صلى الله عليه وسلم
And among them: the satiation of many creatures with his small amount of food, and its multiplication by virtue of his placing his hand in it or his supplication, may Allah bless him and grant him peace.

Commentary
This short passage mentions another miracle: the multiplication of food. The Prophet would feed a large number of people from a small quantity of food, either by his hand touching it or by his supplication. This is a well-known category of miracles (barakah in food), indicating that Allah blessed the provision through the Prophet's intervention.

A) Only his placing his hand
B) Only his supplication
C) Either his hand or his supplication
D) The people's faith

Key Takeaway
The multiplication of food is a prophetic miracle that could occur through the Prophet's hand or his supplication, affirming his prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a situation of scarcity—whether of time, money, or energy—do you instinctively turn to Allah with du'a, or do you first rely on your own planning and worry? What would change in your response if you truly believed that a simple du'a could multiply your provision?
?
The Prophet ﷺ used both his physical action (placing his hand) and his spiritual connection (du'a) to bring about the miracle. In your life, are there areas where you are relying on only one—either only effort or only prayer—without combining both? How can you intentionally unite them starting today?
?
Have you ever experienced a moment of unexpected abundance or sufficiency that you could not explain naturally? Did you recognize it as a potential barakah from Allah, or did you dismiss it as coincidence? What would it mean for your faith to see such moments as signs of prophethood and divine care?
